Its original Serbian language title is Буре барута (Bure baruta) which means Powder Keg. It was released in English speaking countries under the title of Cabaret Balkan, with the official reason for the name change being that Kevin Costner had already registered a film project under the title Powder Keg. The film received a number of distinctions, including a FIPRESCI award at the Venice Film Festival in 1998. It was based on a play by the same title by . The film was selected as the Serbian entry for the Best Foreign Language Film at the 71st Academy Awards, but was not accepted as a nominee.

The film is a biopic based on miracle worker preto velho João de Camargo of Sorocaba and is based on the book João de Camargo de Sorocaba: O Nascimento de uma Religião by Carlos de Campos and Adolfo Frioli. The title comes from a former quilombo, the source of João de Camargo's original spiritual inspiration, located in today's Salto de Pirapora.

Caddyshack is a 1980 American sports comedy film directed by Harold Ramis, written by Brian Doyle-Murray, Ramis and Douglas Kenney, and starring Chevy Chase, Rodney Dangerfield, Ted Knight, Michael O'Keefe and Bill Murray with supporting roles by Sarah Holcomb, Cindy Morgan, and Doyle-Murray. Caddyshack was Ramis's directorial debut and boosted the career of Dangerfield, who was previously known mostly for his stand-up comedy. Grossing nearly $40 million at the domestic box office (the 17th-highest of the year), it was the first of a series of similar comedies. The film has a cult following and was described by ESPN as "perhaps the funniest sports movie ever made." A sequel, Caddyshack II (1988), followed, although only Chase reprised his role and the film was poorly received. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Stevan_Larner <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Harold_Ramis <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Warner_Bros. <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Johnny_Mandel <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Douglas_Kenney <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Rodney_Dangerfield <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Bill_Murray <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Ted_Knight <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Chevy_Chase <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Michael_O'Keefe <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Brian_Doyle-Murray <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Harold_Ramis <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Douglas_Kenney <EOT>

Calibre is a 2018 British thriller film written and directed by Matt Palmer. After a debut at the Edinburgh International Film Festival, it was released on 29 June 2018 on Netflix. It also had a limited release in select Curzon Cinemas in the UK from 21 October to 16 November 2018. The story had been filmed before, in 1924, by William Randolph Hearst's production company, Cosmopolitan, as a silent called The Great White Way, starring Anita Stewart and Oscar Shaw. In this version, Robert Paige introduced the song "I'll Sing You a Thousand Love Songs", with music by Harry Warren and words by Al Dubin, who also wrote "Coney Island", "Here Comes Chiquita", and other songs.

Caesar and Otto's Summer Camp Massacre is a 2009 American comedy slasher film and spoof of the Sleepaway Camp film series, starring Dave Campfield, Paul Chomicki, Felissa Rose, Deron Miller, Joe Estevez, Ken Macfarlane and Brinke Stevens and was written and directed by Dave Campfield, the creator of the original Caesar and Otto film. Caesar and Otto's Summer Camp Massacre made its world premiere on August 15, 2009 at the Fright Night Film Fest in Louisville, Kentucky, where it received a nomination for Best Horror Comedy. It then went on to screen at the Long Island Film Festival on October 9, 2009, where it won Best Editing. It was then screened on June 4, 2010 at the Lighthouse Film Festival, and released on DVD on October 4, 2011. Caesar and Otto's Summer Camp Massacre was the debut feature of Trai Byers who rose to fame in 2015 with the success of Fox's Empire. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Otto's_Summer_Camp_Massacre <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Dave_Campfield <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Otto's_Summer_Camp_Massacre <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Dave_Campfield <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Otto's_Summer_Camp_Massacre <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Dave_Campfield <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Otto's_Summer_Camp_Massacre <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Deron_Miller <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Otto's_Summer_Camp_Massacre <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Brinke_Stevens <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Otto's_Summer_Camp_Massacre <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Felissa_Rose <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Otto's_Summer_Camp_Massacre <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Joe_Estevez <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Otto's_Summer_Camp_Massacre <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Dave_Campfield <EOT>

Cairo Station, also called The Iron Gate (Arabic: باب الحديد Bāb al-Ḥadīd), is a 1958 Egyptian drama film directed by Youssef Chahine. It was entered for competition in the 8th Berlin International Film Festival. The film was selected as the Egyptian entry for the Best Foreign Language Film at the 31st Academy Awards, but was not accepted as a nominee. Since the 1970s, the film has found renewed interest with new generations of international film lovers and has been hailed as a masterpiece in the style of neorealist cinema. Themes depicted in the film include the urban working class, gender-based violence, and sexual repression. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_Station <PRED> dbo:imdbId <OBJ> 0051390 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_Station <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Youssef_Chahine <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_Station <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Egyptian_Arabic <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_Station <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Farid_Shawqi <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_Station <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Hind_Rostom <EOT>

Cabaret is a 1927 American silent crime drama film produced by Famous Players-Lasky, distributed by Paramount Pictures, directed by Robert G. Vignola, and starring Gilda Gray. The film was considered a rival to Paramount's own Underworld released later in 1927. Cabaret is now presumed to be a lost film. It was the winner of the Photoplay award in 1927. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1927_film) <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Harry_Fischbeck <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1927_film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Robert_G._Vignola <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1927_film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Paramount_Pictures <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1927_film) <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Silent_film <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1927_film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Adolph_Zukor <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1927_film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Jesse_L._Lasky <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1927_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Gilda_Gray <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1927_film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Becky_Gardiner <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1927_film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Owen_Davis <EOT>
Café Lumière (珈琲時光, Kōhī Jikō) is a 2003 Japanese film directed by Taiwanese director Hou Hsiao-hsien for Shochiku as homage to Yasujirō Ozu, with direct reference to the late director's Tokyo Story (1953). It premiered at a festival commemorating the centenary of Ozu's birth. It was nominated for a Golden Lion at the 2004 Venice Film Festival. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Lumière <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Mark_Lee_Ping_Bin <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Lumière <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Hou_Hsiao-hsien <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Lumière <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Shochiku <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Lumière <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Liao_Ching-Song <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Lumière <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Yōsui_Inoue <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Lumière <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Hou_Hsiao-hsien <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Lumière <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Chu_T’ien-wen <EOT>

Macy, Anna Kendrick, and Sam Worthington. It debuted in the Special Presentations section of the 2014 Toronto International Film Festival. Cake received mixed reviews and was a box-office bomb, grossing $2.9 million against its $7–10 million budget. However, Aniston's dramatic performance received positive reviews and brought her a nomination at the Golden Globe Awards and another at the Screen Actors Guild Awards.

Calendar Girls is a 2003 British comedy film directed by Nigel Cole. Produced by Touchstone Pictures, it features a screenplay by Tim Firth and Juliette Towhidi, based on a true story of a group of middle-aged Yorkshire women who produced a nude calendar to raise money for Leukaemia Research under the auspices of the Women's Institutes in April 1999 after the husband of one of their members dies from cancer. The film stars an ensemble cast headed by Helen Mirren and Julie Walters, with Linda Bassett, Annette Crosbie, Celia Imrie, Penelope Wilton, Geraldine James, Harriet Thorpe and Philip Glenister playing key supporting roles. Calendar Girls premiered at the Locarno Film Festival and was later shown at Filmfest Hamburg, the Dinard Festival of British Cinema in France, the Warsaw Film Festival, the Tokyo International Film Festival and the UK Film Festival in Hong Kong. It garnered generally positive reactions by film critics, who compared it with another British comedy film The Full Monty (1997). At a budget of $10 million it also became a major commercial success, eventually grossing $93.4 million worldwide following its theatrical release in the U.S. In addition, the picture was awarded the British Comedy Award for Best Comedy Film, and received ALFS Award, Empire Award and Satellite Award nominations for Mirren and Walters, and a Golden Globe Award nomination for Mirren. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Nigel_Cole <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Walt_Disney_Studios_Motion_Pictures <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Patrick_Doyle <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Julie_Walters <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Penelope_Wilton <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Annette_Crosbie <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Linda_Bassett <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Celia_Imrie <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Harriet_Thorpe <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Helen_Mirren <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Tim_Firth <EOT>

Cairo is a 1963 American crime film directed by Wolf Rilla and written by Joan LaCour Scott. The film stars George Sanders, Richard Johnson, Faten Hamama, John Meillon, Ahmed Mazhar, Eric Pohlmann and the director's father Walter Rilla. The film was released on August 21, 1963, by Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer. The film is a nearly scene-by-scene remake of John Huston's The Asphalt Jungle. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1963_film) <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Desmond_Dickinson <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1963_film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Wolf_Rilla <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1963_film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1963_film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Bernard_Gribble <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1963_film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Kenneth_V._Jones <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1963_film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Lawrence_Bachmann <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1963_film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Ronald_Kinnoch <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1963_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Richard_Johnson_(actor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1963_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:George_Sanders <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1963_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Ahmed_Mazhar <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1963_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Eric_Pohlmann <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1963_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Faten_Hamama <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1963_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:John_Meillon <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1963_film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Joan_LaCour_Scott <EOT>

Caesar Must Die (Italian: Cesare deve morire) is a 2012 Italian drama film directed by Paolo and Vittorio Taviani. The film competed at the 62nd Berlin International Film Festival where it won the Golden Bear. The film is set in Rebibbia Prison (suburb of Rome), and follows convicts in their rehearsals ahead of a prison performance of Julius Caesar. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_Must_Die <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Paolo_and_Vittorio_Taviani <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_Must_Die <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Roberto_Perpignani <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_Must_Die <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Giuliano_Taviani <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_Must_Die <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Grazia_Volpi <EOT>
<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1942_film) <PRED> dbo:imdbId <OBJ> 0034565 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1942_film) <PRED> dbo:releaseDate <OBJ> 1942-08-17 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1942_film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:W._S._Van_Dyke <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1942_film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:James_E._Newcom <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1942_film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Herbert_Stothart <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1942_film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Joseph_L._Mankiewicz <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1942_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Robert_Young_(actor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1942_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jeanette_MacDonald <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1942_film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Ladislas_Fodor <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Cairo is a 1942 musical comedy film made by MGM and Loew's, and directed by W. S. Van Dyke. The screenplay was written by John McClain, based on an idea by Ladislas Fodor about a news reporter shipwrecked in a torpedo attack, who teams up with a Hollywood singer and her maid to foil Nazi spies. The music score is by Herbert Stothart. This film was Jeanette MacDonald's last film on her MGM contract. The film was poorly received upon its initial release.

Cake is a Nollywood romantic comedy film directed by Prosper Edesiri and produced by Tongryang Pantu. It stars Saskay, Patience Ozokwor, Emmanuel Jibunor, Philip Asaya, Tope Tedela, Sophie Alakija, Folu Storms with Dotun Olakunri as the Executive Producer and also Steve Gukas Co-producer of the film. It was released through Natives Filmworks and Michelangelo Productions on the Natives Family Friendly Films Project Production Company. The film was distributed through FilmOne Production and was theatrically released on 25 February 2022. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cake_(2022_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Patience_Ozokwor <EOT>

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Paradis <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Bodil_Ipsen <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Paradis <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Lau_Lauritzen_Jr. <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Paradis <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Marie_Ejlersen <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Paradis <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Denmark <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Paradis <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Sven_Gyldmark <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Paradis <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Poul_Reichhardt <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Paradis <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Ib_Schønberg <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Paradis <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Johannes_Allen <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Café Paradis (English Title: Paradise Cafe) is a 1950 Danish film, directed by Bodil Ipsen and Lau Lauritzen Jr., and written by . The film received the Bodil Award for Best Danish Film, and Ib Schønberg, for what is regarded his finest performance, received the Bodil Award for Best Supporting Actor. The story illuminates the problems of alcoholism as it follows the lives of two people: one is a common workman (played by Poul Reichhardt) who drinks too much beer, and the other is a company director (played by Ib Schønberg), who believes he just needs "a little one every now and then." They both come to face the consequences of their addictions.

Calamity Anne's Love Affair is a 1914 American silent short Western directed by Tom Ricketts starring Charlotte Burton and Louise Lester as Calamity Anne. Also starring George Field, Edith Borella and B. Reeves Eason. Café Flesh is a 1982 post-apocalyptic cult pornographic science fiction film designed and directed by Stephen Sayadian (under the pseudonym "Rinse Dream") and co-written by Sayadian and Jerry Stahl (credited as "Herbert W. Day"). Music was composed and produced by noted music producer Mitchell Froom (and later appeared in his album, Key of Cool). Two sequels, Café Flesh 2 and Café Flesh 3, were released in 1997 and 2003, without the participation of the original creators. The sequels were written and directed by Antonio Passolini and did not have the same degree of popularity and cult appeal as the first film. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Flesh <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Stephen_Sayadian <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Flesh <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:VCA_Pictures <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Flesh <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Sidney_Katz <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Flesh <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:English_language <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Flesh <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Mitchell_Froom <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Flesh <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Stephen_Sayadian <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Flesh <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Stephen_Sayadian <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Flesh <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Jerry_Stahl <EOT>

Calendar Girls is a 2015 Indian drama film directed by Madhur Bhandarkar and co-produced by Sangeeta Ahir and Bhandarkar Entertainment. Akanksha Puri played a main female lead role. The film's music was composed by Meet Bros Anjjan and Amaal Mallik. The film released on 25 September 2015. <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Otto's_Summer_Camp_Massacre <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Dave_Campfield <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Otto's_Summer_Camp_Massacre <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Dave_Campfield <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Otto's_Summer_Camp_Massacre <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Dave_Campfield <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Otto's_Summer_Camp_Massacre <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Deron_Miller <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Otto's_Summer_Camp_Massacre <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Brinke_Stevens <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Otto's_Summer_Camp_Massacre <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Felissa_Rose <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Otto's_Summer_Camp_Massacre <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Joe_Estevez <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Otto's_Summer_Camp_Massacre <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Dave_Campfield <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Caesar and Otto's Summer Camp Massacre is a 2009 American comedy slasher film and spoof of the Sleepaway Camp film series, starring Dave Campfield, Paul Chomicki, Felissa Rose, Deron Miller, Joe Estevez, Ken Macfarlane and Brinke Stevens and was written and directed by Dave Campfield, the creator of the original Caesar and Otto film. Caesar and Otto's Summer Camp Massacre made its world premiere on August 15, 2009 at the Fright Night Film Fest in Louisville, Kentucky, where it received a nomination for Best Horror Comedy. It then went on to screen at the Long Island Film Festival on October 9, 2009, where it won Best Editing. It was then screened on June 4, 2010 at the Lighthouse Film Festival, and released on DVD on October 4, 2011. Caesar and Otto's Summer Camp Massacre was the debut feature of Trai Byers who rose to fame in 2015 with the success of Fox's Empire.

Cafe Noir (Korean: 카페 느와르; RR: Ka-pe-neu-wa-reu) is a 2009 South Korean romance melodrama film starring Shin Ha-kyun, Moon Jeong-hee, Kim Hye-na and Jung Yu-mi. Written and directed by first-time director Jung Sung-il, a well regarded film critic-turned-director, it is a contemplation on love and heartbreak largely based on two works of literature - Johann Wolfgang von Goethe's The Sorrows of Young Werther and Fyodor Dostoyevsky's White Nights. The critically acclaimed work debuted at the 66th Venice Film Festival in 2009, and Jung was nominated for New Talent Grand Pix at the 2010 Copenhagen International Film Festival. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Noir <PRED> dbo:country <OBJ> dbr:South_Korea <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Noir <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Jung_Sung-il_(director) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Noir <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jung_Yu-mi_(actress_born_1983) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Noir <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Moon_Jeong-hee <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Noir <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Shin_Ha-kyun <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Noir <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Jung_Sung-il_(director) <EOT>

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Flesh <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Stephen_Sayadian <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Flesh <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:VCA_Pictures <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Flesh <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Sidney_Katz <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Flesh <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:English_language <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Flesh <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Mitchell_Froom <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Flesh <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Stephen_Sayadian <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Flesh <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Stephen_Sayadian <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Flesh <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Jerry_Stahl <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Café Flesh is a 1982 post-apocalyptic cult pornographic science fiction film designed and directed by Stephen Sayadian (under the pseudonym "Rinse Dream") and co-written by Sayadian and Jerry Stahl (credited as "Herbert W. Day"). Music was composed and produced by noted music producer Mitchell Froom (and later appeared in his album, Key of Cool). Two sequels, Café Flesh 2 and Café Flesh 3, were released in 1997 and 2003, without the participation of the original creators. The sequels were written and directed by Antonio Passolini and did not have the same degree of popularity and cult appeal as the first film.

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cactus_Flower_(film) <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Charles_Lang <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cactus_Flower_(film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Gene_Saks <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cactus_Flower_(film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Columbia_Pictures <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cactus_Flower_(film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Maury_Winetrobe <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cactus_Flower_(film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Quincy_Jones <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cactus_Flower_(film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Mike_Frankovich <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cactus_Flower_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Goldie_Hawn <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cactus_Flower_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Walter_Matthau <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cactus_Flower_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Ingrid_Bergman <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cactus_Flower_(film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:I._A._L._Diamond <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Cactus Flower is a 1969 American screwball comedy film directed by Gene Saks and starring Walter Matthau, Ingrid Bergman, and Goldie Hawn, who won an Academy Award for her performance. Along with Hello Dolly!, are the movies that end the Golden Age of Hollywood.[citation?] The screenplay was adapted by I. A. L. Diamond from the 1965 Broadway play of the same name written by Abe Burrows, which in turn was based upon the French play Fleur de cactus by Pierre Barillet and Jean-Pierre Gredy. Cactus Flower was the ninth highest-grossing film of 1969.

Directed by Allan Arkush and written by Harold Ramis (who co-wrote and directed the original Caddyshack) and PJ Torokvei, it stars Jackie Mason, Robert Stack, Dyan Cannon, Dina Merrill, Jonathan Silverman, Brian McNamara, Marsha Warfield, Paul Bartel, and Randy Quaid with special appearances by Chevy Chase and Dan Aykroyd. While the writing of the film is officially credited to Ramis and Torokvei, the first-draft script by Ramis and Torokvei was rewritten by other uncredited writers. The sequel was panned by critics and is considered one of the worst sequels of all time. However, Kenny Loggins' "Nobody's Fool" which was used as the film's theme song was a chart success where it hit #8 on the Billboard Hot 100.

Cake is a 2014 American drama film directed by Daniel Barnz, written by Patrick Tobin, and starring Jennifer Aniston, Adriana Barraza, Felicity Huffman, William H. Macy, Anna Kendrick, and Sam Worthington. It debuted in the Special Presentations section of the 2014 Toronto International Film Festival. Cake received mixed reviews and was a box-office bomb, grossing $2.9 million against its $7–10 million budget. It stars Jesse Eisenberg, Kristen Stewart, Steve Carell, Jeannie Berlin, Blake Lively, Parker Posey, Corey Stoll, and Ken Stott. The plot follows a young man who moves to Hollywood in the 1930s, where he falls in love with the assistant to his uncle, a powerful talent agent. The film had its premiere at the Cannes Film Festival on May 11, 2016, and was theatrically released in the United States on July 15, 2016, by Amazon Studios and Lionsgate. It received generally positive reviews and grossed $43 million. It received nomination at the Golden Eagle Award in 2017 for Best Foreign Language Film.

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caballo_prieto_azabache_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jaime_Fernández_(actor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caballo_prieto_azabache_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Antonio_Aguilar <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caballo_prieto_azabache_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Flor_Silvestre <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Caballo prieto azabache (La tumba de Villa) is a 1968 Mexican historical drama film starring Antonio Aguilar, Flor Silvestre, and Jaime Fernández. It focuses on a horse breeder named Jesús who is set on buying a horse known as "Caballo prieto" (dark horse) and pursuing a relationship with a singer named Genoveva Alarios. With he and Genoveva eventually recruited as spies for the revolutionary leader Pancho Villa. The film was successful at the box-office and stayed in theaters for a surprising nine weeks.

It premiered on 10 May 2004, replacing Chocolate com Pimenta, and ended on 20 November 2004, replaced by Como uma Onda. The telenovela is written by Ricardo Waddington, with the collaboration of Edmara Barbosa and Edilene Barbosa. It is based on the 1979 telenovela of the same name and originally shown on Rede Globo. It stars Vanessa Giácomo, Daniel de Oliveira, Tony Ramos, Patrícia Pillar, Mauro Mendonça, Carolina Kasting, Regiane Alves, Danton Mello, Eriberto Leão, Maria Flor and Malvino Salvador in the leading roles.

The film stars Dileep, Meera Jasmine, Indrajith and Vimala Raman. The music is by Debojyoti Mishra. The film deals with the issue of trafficking in women and how an Orphan girl from Kerala gets caught in it. It showcased Blessy's yet another different genre film and successfully provided Dileep a different character unlike his usual comic characters.

Cabaret Balkan is a 1998 Serbian film directed by Goran Paskaljević starring Miki Manojlović and Nebojša Glogovac. Its original Serbian language title is Буре барута (Bure baruta) which means Powder Keg. It was released in English speaking countries under the title of Cabaret Balkan, with the official reason for the name change being that Kevin Costner had already registered a film project under the title Powder Keg. The film received a number of distinctions, including a FIPRESCI award at the Venice Film Festival in 1998. It was based on a play by the same title by . The film was selected as the Serbian entry for the Best Foreign Language Film at the 71st Academy Awards, but was not accepted as a nominee. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_Balkan <PRED> dbo:imdbId <OBJ> 0169145 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_Balkan <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Milan_Spasić <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_Balkan <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Goran_Paskaljević <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_Balkan <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:StudioCanal <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_Balkan <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Zoran_Simjanović <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_Balkan <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Goran_Paskaljević <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_Balkan <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Martine_de_Clermont-Tonnerre <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_Balkan <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Bata_Živojinović <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_Balkan <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Bogdan_Diklić <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_Balkan <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Mirjana_Karanović <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_Balkan <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Dragan_Nikolić <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_Balkan <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Miki_Manojlović <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_Balkan <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Nebojša_Glogovac <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_Balkan <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Sergej_Trifunović <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_Balkan <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Goran_Paskaljević <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_Balkan <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Filip_David <EOT>

Cain and Mabel is a 1936 romantic comedy film designed as a vehicle for Marion Davies in which she co-stars with Clark Gable. The story had been filmed before, in 1924, by William Randolph Hearst's production company, Cosmopolitan, as a silent called The Great White Way, starring Anita Stewart and Oscar Shaw. In this version, Robert Paige introduced the song "I'll Sing You a Thousand Love Songs", with music by Harry Warren and words by Al Dubin, who also wrote "Coney Island", "Here Comes Chiquita", and other songs. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Mabel <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:George_Barnes_(cinematographer) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Mabel <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Lloyd_Bacon <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Mabel <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Warner_Bros. <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Mabel <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:William_Holmes_(film_editor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Mabel <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:English_language <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Mabel <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Bernhard_Kaun <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Mabel <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Al_Dubin <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Mabel <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Harry_Warren <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Mabel <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Heinz_Eric_Roemheld <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Mabel <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Hal_B._Wallis <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Mabel <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Jack_L._Warner <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Mabel <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Robert_Paige <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Mabel <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Clark_Gable <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Mabel <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Allen_Jenkins <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Mabel <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Marion_Davies <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Mabel <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Laird_Doyle <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Mabel <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:H.C._Witwer <EOT>

Caine's Arcade is an 11-minute short documentary film by Nirvan Mullick released on April 9, 2012 that features a cardboard arcade created by then 9-year-old Caine Monroy out of boxes and everyday objects. The boy ran his arcade from his father's auto parts store in East Los Angeles mid-2011. Nirvan was inspired to make the documentary after unexpectedly coming across the arcade while getting a door handle for his car. Nirvan became Caine's first customer, purchasing a $2 Fun Pass, and decided to make a film about Caine's Arcade after witnessing the level of commitment, work, and thought Caine had put into the arcade. After learning he had been Caine's first and only customer, Nirvan used social media to arrange a surprise flash mob of customers to come to play Caine's Arcade, which was included in the film. After being uploaded on YouTube, the short film soon became a viral video, and numerous people donated money towards a college fund that Nirvan had established for Caine. Since the film's release, schools around the world have recreated similar cardboard arcades, and the positive response inspired Nirvan and the team to start the Imagination Foundation, a non-profit aimed at fostering creativity and entrepreneurship in adults across the world. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caine's_Arcade <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Nirvan_Mullick <EOT>

Cabocla is a Brazilian telenovela produced and broadcast by Rede Globo. It premiered on 10 May 2004, replacing Chocolate com Pimenta, and ended on 20 November 2004, replaced by Como uma Onda. The telenovela is written by Ricardo Waddington, with the collaboration of Edmara Barbosa and Edilene Barbosa. It is based on the 1979 telenovela of the same name and originally shown on Rede Globo. It stars Vanessa Giácomo, Daniel de Oliveira, Tony Ramos, Patrícia Pillar, Mauro Mendonça, Carolina Kasting, Regiane Alves, Danton Mello, Eriberto Leão, Maria Flor and Malvino Salvador in the leading roles. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabocla <PRED> dbo:releaseDate <OBJ> 2004-05-10 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabocla <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Carolina_Kasting <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabocla <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Patrícia_Pillar <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabocla <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Regiane_Alves <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabocla <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Reginaldo_Faria <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabocla <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Vanessa_Giácomo <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabocla <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Vera_Holtz <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabocla <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Mauro_Mendonça <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabocla <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Malvino_Salvador <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabocla <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Tony_Ramos <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabocla <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Daniel_de_Oliveira_(actor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabocla <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Danton_Mello <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabocla <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Eriberto_Leão <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabocla <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Othon_Bastos <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabocla <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Otávio_Augusto <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabocla <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jussara_Freire <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabocla <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Maria_Flor <EOT>

Cala, My Dog! is a 2003 Chinese comedy film directed by Lu Xuechang. The film had its world premiere at the 2003 Berlin International Film Festival and its Chinese release a week earlier on February 2, 2003. The film follows a blue-collar worker (Ge You) in Beijing as he attempts to acquire a dog license in 18 hours for his beloved unlicensed Cala. The film was co-produced by the successful film director Feng Xiaogang. Though a comedy, Cala, My Dog! moves at a subdued pace. The film stars George Sanders, Richard Johnson, Faten Hamama, John Meillon, Ahmed Mazhar, Eric Pohlmann and the director's father Walter Rilla. The film was released on August 21, 1963, by Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer. The film is a nearly scene-by-scene remake of John Huston's The Asphalt Jungle.

Cadet Girl is a 1941 comedy film directed by Ray McCarey and written by Stanley Rauh and H.W. Hanemann. The film stars Carole Landis, George Montgomery, Shepperd Strudwick, William Tracy, Janis Carter and Robert Lowery. The film was released on November 28, 1941, by 20th Century Fox. Cabeza de Vaca is a 1991 Mexican film about the adventures of Álvar Núñez Cabeza de Vaca (c. 1490 – c. 1557), an early Spanish explorer, as he traversed what later became the American South. He was one of four survivors of the Narváez expedition and shipwreck. He became known as a shaman among the Native American tribes he encountered, which helped him survive. His journey of a number of years began in 1528. After his return to Spain, he published his journal in 1542. The screenplay by Guillermo Sheridan and Nicolás Echevarría is based on this journal. Directed by Nicolás Echevarría and starring Juan Diego, the film was entered into the 41st Berlin International Film Festival. The film was selected as the Mexican entry for the Best Foreign Language Film at the 63rd Academy Awards, but was not accepted as a nominee. A DVD version was released in 2012. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabeza_de_Vaca_(film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Nicolás_Echevarría <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabeza_de_Vaca_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Juan_Diego_(actor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabeza_de_Vaca_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Daniel_Giménez_Cacho <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabeza_de_Vaca_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Roberto_Sosa_(actor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabeza_de_Vaca_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Carlos_Castañón <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabeza_de_Vaca_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Gerardo_Villarreal <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabeza_de_Vaca_(film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Álvar_Núñez_Cabeza_de_Vaca <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabeza_de_Vaca_(film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Guillermo_Sheridan <EOT>

Cal is a 1984 Irish drama film directed by Pat O'Connor and starring John Lynch and Helen Mirren. <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calais-Dover_(film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:L'Alliance_Cinématographique_Européenne <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calais-Dover_(film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Aleksandr_Uralsky <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calais-Dover_(film) <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:French_language <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calais-Dover_(film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Mischa_Spoliansky <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Calais-Dover (French: Calais-Douvres) is a 1931 French-German comedy film directed by Jean Boyer and Anatole Litvak and starring Lilian Harvey, André Roanne and Armand Bernard. It is the French-language version of the German film No More Love, with Harvey reprising her role. The title refers to the Dover–Calais ferry. It incorporated location shooting on the French Riviera with interiors shot at the Babelsberg Studios in Berlin. The film's sets were designed by the art directors Robert Herlth, Walter Röhrig and Werner Schlichting.

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cake_(2018_film) <PRED> <MASK> <OBJ> dbr:Sayed_Zulfiqar_Abbas_Bukhari <EOT>	dbo:producer
Caballerango (Horse Wrangler) is a 2018 Mexican documentary film, director Juan Pablo González's debut feature. It's a portrait of residents of Milpillas in Los Altos de Jalisco as they grapple with the sudden death of a young horse wrangler named Nando. The editing alternates wide shots of landscape and community with more intimate scenes where the director, a native of the region himself, asks questions of those onscreen. Gradually, Nando's death starts to look like it might have been a suicide. It also becomes clear that the community's still reeling from the loss of several other young people. The mysterious circumstances of their demise dovetail with globalization's effects on the community: a drop in farming jobs and population exodus from the region. The film expands upon material that González's Cannes Critics' Week short, "¿Por qué el recuerdo?" ("The Solitude of Memory"), previously broached. It displays dimensions of slow cinema and includes only 37 shots across its 62-minute duration. The film's production occurred between 2013 and 2017, and it received support from the Sundance Institute, the Ford Foundation, the Austin Film Society, and the California Institute of the Arts, where González is a professor. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caballerango <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Juan_Pablo_González <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caballerango <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Mubi_(streaming_service) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caballerango <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Isidore_Bethel <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caballerango <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Juan_Pablo_González <EOT>

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:imdbId <OBJ> 0074263 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:releaseDate <OBJ> 1976-04-01 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Peter_James_(cinematographer) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Donald_Crombie <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Roadshow_Entertainment <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Anthony_Buckley <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Helen_Morse <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jack_Thompson_(actor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jacki_Weaver <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Joan_Long <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Caddie is an Australian film biopic directed by Donald Crombie and produced by Anthony Buckley. Released on 1 April 1976, it is representative of the Australian film renaissance which occurred during that decade. Set mainly in Sydney during the 1920s and 1930s, including the Great Depression, it portrays the life of a young middle class woman struggling to raise two children after her marriage breaks up. Based on Caddie, the Story of a Barmaid, a partly fictitious autobiography of Catherine Beatrice "Caddie" Edmonds, it made Helen Morse a local star and earned Jacki Weaver and Melissa Jaffer each an Australian Film Institute Award.

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:imdbId <OBJ> 0072756 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Buzz_Kulik <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Sony_Pictures_Television <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Robert_Mintz <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Buzz_Kulik <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Sam_Bottoms <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Anne_Bloom <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Katherine_Helmond <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Lani_O'Grady <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Susan_Dey <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Cage Without a Key is a 1975 American made-for-television drama film directed by Buzz Kulik and starring Susan Dey and Sam Bottoms, with Jonelle Allen and Lani O'Grady in supporting roles. The film premiered on the CBS television network the evening of March 14, 1975, later repeating at various times on The CBS Late Movie. The film was released on VHS under the title Imprisoned Women. Cage Without a Key was filmed at Las Palmas School for Girls in Commerce, California, now known as the Dorothy Kirby Center. It was a juvenile detention center, not an actual women's prison. Many of the extras were actual inmates.

Caesar and Cleopatra is a 1945 British Technicolor film directed by Gabriel Pascal and starring Vivien Leigh and Claude Rains. Some scenes were directed by Brian Desmond Hurst, who took no formal credit. The picture was adapted from the play Caesar and Cleopatra (1901) by George Bernard Shaw, produced by Independent Producers and Pascal Film Productions and distributed by Eagle-Lion Distributors. Upon release, Caesar and Cleopatra failed to earn back its colossal budget. John Bryan was nominated for an Oscar for Best Art Direction. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Cleopatra_(film) <PRED> dbo:releaseDate <OBJ> 1945-12-11 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Cleopatra_(film) <PRED> dbo:releaseDate <OBJ> 1946-09-06 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Cleopatra_(film) <PRED> dbo:releaseDate <OBJ> 1946-09-16 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Cleopatra_(film) <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Freddie_Young <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Cleopatra_(film) <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Jack_Cardiff <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Cleopatra_(film) <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Jack_Hildyard <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Cleopatra_(film) <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Robert_Krasker <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Cleopatra_(film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Gabriel_Pascal <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Cleopatra_(film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:United_Artists <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Cleopatra_(film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Eagle-Lion_Films <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Cleopatra_(film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Joan_Warwick <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Cleopatra_(film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Frederick_Wilson_(film_editor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Cleopatra_(film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Georges_Auric <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Cleopatra_(film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Gabriel_Pascal <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Cleopatra_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Vivien_Leigh <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Cleopatra_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Claude_Rains <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Cleopatra_(film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:George_Bernard_Shaw <EOT>

The film takes its title from the short story collection of the same name by Giorgio Scerbanenco, and is partially based on three of its stories. The musical score was composed by Luis Enriquez Bacalov and performed by the progressive rock band Osanna. Caliber 9 is the first part in Di Leo's Milieu Trilogy of poliziotteschi films. It was followed by La mala ordina (The Italian Connection) in 1972 and Il Boss (The Boss) in 1973.
California Firebrand is a 1948 American Western film directed by Philip Ford and written by J. Benton Cheney, John K. Butler and Royal K. Cole. The film stars Monte Hale, Lorna Gray, Paul Hurst, Alice Tyrrell, Tristram Coffin and LeRoy Mason. Cadet Holiday is an 11-minute 1951 Canadian documentary film, made by the National Film Board of Canada (NFB) as part of the postwar Canada Carries On series. The film, directed by David Bairstow, Robert Humble and Douglas Wilkinson, was produced by Sydney Newman and Michael Spencer. Cadet Holiday was an account of a Canadian Army Cadet during a summer camp. The film's French version title is Cadets en vacances. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadet_Holiday <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:David_Bairstow_(director) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadet_Holiday <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Columbia_Pictures <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadet_Holiday <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Robert_Fleming_(composer) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadet_Holiday <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Michael_Spencer_(producer) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadet_Holiday <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Sydney_Newman <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadet_Holiday <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:David_Bairstow_(director) <EOT>

Cafe Mascot is a 1936 British comedy film directed by Lawrence Huntington and starring Geraldine Fitzgerald. It was produced by Gabriel Pascal, and made at Wembley Studios. A young man discovers £1,000 in a taxi. The plot of the film centers on car salesman Joey O'Brien (Williams) whose life is consumed by turmoil, which all comes to a head when his dealership is taken hostage by Larry (Robbins), a crazed motorcyclist. The film received mixed reviews from critics but performed above its production budget at the box office, grossing $27.6 million against its $15 million budget.

Caché (French: [kaʃe]), also known as Hidden (United Kingdom), is a 2005 psychological thriller film written and directed by Michael Haneke and starring Daniel Auteuil and Juliette Binoche. The plot follows an upper-middle-class French couple, Georges (Auteuil) and Anne (Binoche), who are terrorised by anonymous tapes that appear on their front porch and seem to show the family is under surveillance. Clues in the videos point to Georges's childhood memories, and his resistance to his parents' adopting an Algerian orphan named Majid, who was sent away. The tapes lead him to the now-grown Majid (Maurice Bénichou). Shot in Paris and Vienna in 2004, the film is an international co-production of France, Austria, Germany and Italy. Haneke wrote the screenplay with Auteuil and Binoche in mind, and with a concept of exploring guilt and childhood. When he learned of the French government's decades-long denial of the 1961 Seine River massacre, he incorporated memories of the event into his story. Caché opened at the 2005 Cannes Film Festival to critical acclaim for the performances and Haneke's direction. Its plot ambiguities raised considerable discussion. The film has been interpreted as an allegory about collective guilt and collective memory, and as a statement on France's Algerian War and colonialism in general. While presented as a mystery, the film does not explicitly reveal which character sends the tapes. Haneke regarded that as of secondary importance to the exploration of guilt and left the question up to viewer interpretation. The film won three awards at Cannes, including Best Director; five European Film Awards, including Best Film; and other honours. It was controversially disqualified for the Academy Award for Best Foreign Language Film. The film, directed by David Bairstow, Robert Humble and Douglas Wilkinson, was produced by Sydney Newman and Michael Spencer. Cadet Holiday was an account of a Canadian Army Cadet during a summer camp. The film's French version title is Cadets en vacances.

Cain's Cutthroats is a 1971 western-themed exploitation film. It is a story of brutality, betrayal, and revenge set in the period immediately following the end of the American Civil War. The film was released under the alternate titles Cain's Way, The Blood Seekers, and Justice Cain. The film is also known as Star Dust and Sweet Music (American reissue title). The movie was written by Lee Loeb, Mary Loos, and Richard Sale, with a cast featuring Jane Frazee, William Marshall, Gail Patrick, Kenny Baker and Victor McLaglen. This was Patrick's last film before retiring from acting in the wake of her marriage.

The film had its world premiere at the 2003 Berlin International Film Festival and its Chinese release a week earlier on February 2, 2003. The film follows a blue-collar worker (Ge You) in Beijing as he attempts to acquire a dog license in 18 hours for his beloved unlicensed Cala. The film was co-produced by the successful film director Feng Xiaogang. Though a comedy, Cala, My Dog! moves at a subdued pace. Despite this, during its world premiere in Berlin, sales agents from Celestial Pictures billed the film as a more zany, traditional comedy.

Caddie is an Australian film biopic directed by Donald Crombie and produced by Anthony Buckley. Released on 1 April 1976, it is representative of the Australian film renaissance which occurred during that decade. Set mainly in Sydney during the 1920s and 1930s, including the Great Depression, it portrays the life of a young middle class woman struggling to raise two children after her marriage breaks up. Based on Caddie, the Story of a Barmaid, a partly fictitious autobiography of Catherine Beatrice "Caddie" Edmonds, it made Helen Morse a local star and earned Jacki Weaver and Melissa Jaffer each an Australian Film Institute Award. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:imdbId <OBJ> 0074263 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:releaseDate <OBJ> 1976-04-01 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Peter_James_(cinematographer) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Donald_Crombie <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Roadshow_Entertainment <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Anthony_Buckley <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Helen_Morse <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jack_Thompson_(actor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jacki_Weaver <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddie_(film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Joan_Long <EOT>

Cain (German: Kain) is a 1918 German silent drama film directed by and and produced by Max Maschke. In the starring roles were Erich Kaiser-Titz, Olga Engl and Reinhold Schünzel. <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:IFC_Midnight <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Kevin_Riepl <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Matthew_Daddario <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Gage_Golightly <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Dustin_Ingram <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Eli_Roth <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Cabin Fever is a 2016 American science fiction horror film directed by Travis Zariwny (under the pseudonym Travis Z) and written by Eli Roth. A remake of Roth's 2002 film of the same name and the fourth installment in the Cabin Fever series, the film stars Samuel Davis, Gage Golightly, Matthew Daddario, Nadine Crocker, and Dustin Ingram. The film was released on February 12, 2016, by IFC Midnight. Eli Roth, writer and director of the original film, acts as co-writer and executive producer. The film was poorly received by critics and underperformed at the box office.

Cabin Pressure (also known as Hijack'd and Autopilot) is a 2002 Canadian action film. The television film was broadcast in 2003 and released to home media shortly after. Cabin Pressure reunited Craig Sheffer and John Pyper-Ferguson (who appeared together in the 1994 movie Roadflower). <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caché_(film) <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Christian_Berger <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caché_(film) <PRED> dbo:country <OBJ> dbr:Cinema_of_Austria <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caché_(film) <PRED> dbo:country <OBJ> dbr:Cinema_of_France <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caché_(film) <PRED> dbo:country <OBJ> dbr:Cinema_of_Germany <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caché_(film) <PRED> dbo:country <OBJ> dbr:Cinema_of_Italy <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caché_(film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Michael_Haneke <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caché_(film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Les_films_du_losange <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caché_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Bernard_Le_Coq <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caché_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Denis_Podalydès <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caché_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Juliette_Binoche <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caché_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Annie_Girardot <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caché_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Daniel_Auteuil <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caché_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Daniel_Duval <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caché_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Nathalie_Richard <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caché_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Maurice_Bénichou <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caché_(film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Michael_Haneke <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Caché (French: [kaʃe]), also known as Hidden (United Kingdom), is a 2005 psychological thriller film written and directed by Michael Haneke and starring Daniel Auteuil and Juliette Binoche. The plot follows an upper-middle-class French couple, Georges (Auteuil) and Anne (Binoche), who are terrorised by anonymous tapes that appear on their front porch and seem to show the family is under surveillance. Clues in the videos point to Georges's childhood memories, and his resistance to his parents' adopting an Algerian orphan named Majid, who was sent away. The tapes lead him to the now-grown Majid (Maurice Bénichou). Shot in Paris and Vienna in 2004, the film is an international co-production of France, Austria, Germany and Italy. Haneke wrote the screenplay with Auteuil and Binoche in mind, and with a concept of exploring guilt and childhood. When he learned of the French government's decades-long denial of the 1961 Seine River massacre, he incorporated memories of the event into his story. Caché opened at the 2005 Cannes Film Festival to critical acclaim for the performances and Haneke's direction. Its plot ambiguities raised considerable discussion. The film has been interpreted as an allegory about collective guilt and collective memory, and as a statement on France's Algerian War and colonialism in general. While presented as a mystery, the film does not explicitly reveal which character sends the tapes. Haneke regarded that as of secondary importance to the exploration of guilt and left the question up to viewer interpretation. The film won three awards at Cannes, including Best Director; five European Film Awards, including Best Film; and other honours. It was controversially disqualified for the Academy Award for Best Foreign Language Film. Caché has been regarded in the years since its release as one of the greatest films of the 2000s, included in BBC's 100 Greatest Films of the 21st Century.

Cain and Abel (Filipino: Cain at Abel) is a 1982 Philippine action thriller drama film directed by Lino Brocka from a written story and screenplay by Ricardo "Ricky" Lee. The film's story was inspired by the Biblical story of two brothers, Christopher de Leon and Phillip Salvador respectively played the roles of Ellis and Lorenzo, the two brothers and sons of Senyora Pina (Mona Lisa), who have different views on each other. However, the sibling rivalry became violent and bloody due to the issue of inheritance of their family land and Senyora Pina's favoritism to her younger son. It also stars Carmi Martin as Zita, Ellis's fiancée from Manila; Cecille Castillo as Rina, the house helper, and Ellis's other woman; and Baby Delgado as Becky, Lorenzo's wife. Cain at Abel was released on October 8, 1982, by Cine Suerte Inc., it served as the first Filipino film entry for the San Sebastián International Film Festival in Spain in the same year, and received accolades from award-giving bodies for cinema. The film was digitally restored and remastered by ABS-CBN Film Restoration Project and Central Digital Lab in 2016; the restored version was premiered on August 11, 2016. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Abel_(1982_film) <PRED> dbo:country <OBJ> dbr:Philippines <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Abel_(1982_film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Lino_Brocka <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Abel_(1982_film) <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:English_language <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Abel_(1982_film) <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Filipino_language <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Abel_(1982_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Carmi_Martin <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Abel_(1982_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Christopher_de_Leon <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Abel_(1982_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Mona_Lisa_(actress) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Abel_(1982_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Phillip_Salvador <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Abel_(1982_film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Ricky_Lee <EOT>

Calendar Girl is a 1947 American musical-romance film directed by Allan Dwan. The film is also known as Star Dust and Sweet Music (American reissue title). The movie was written by Lee Loeb, Mary Loos, and Richard Sale, with a cast featuring Jane Frazee, William Marshall, Gail Patrick, Kenny Baker and Victor McLaglen. <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caffè_Italia,_Montréal <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Paul_Tana <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caffè_Italia,_Montréal <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Tony_Nardi <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caffè_Italia,_Montréal <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Pierre_Curzi <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caffè_Italia,_Montréal <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Paul_Tana <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Caffè Italia, Montréal is a Canadian docudrama film, directed by Paul Tana and released in 1985. Focusing on the Italian Canadian community in Montreal, Quebec, the film profiles the community's history through a mix of archival footage and historical reenactments of key events acted by a cast led by Pierre Curzi and Tony Nardi. The film won the Prix L.-E.-Ouimet-Molson from the Association québécoise des critiques de cinéma for 1985.

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Eugenio_Bava <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Segundo_de_Chomon <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Giovanni_Pastrone <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Silent_film <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Intertitles <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Ildebrando_Pizzetti <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Manlio_Mazza <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Giovanni_Pastrone <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Bartolomeo_Pagano <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Gabriele_D'Annunzio <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Giovanni_Pastrone <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Cabiria is a 1914 Italian epic silent film, directed by Giovanni Pastrone and shot in Turin. The film is set in ancient Sicily, Carthage, and Cirta during the period of the Second Punic War (218–202 BC). It follows a melodramatic main plot about an abducted little girl, Cabiria, and features an eruption of Mount Etna, heinous religious rituals in Carthage, the alpine trek of Hannibal, Archimedes' defeat of the Roman fleet at the Siege of Syracuse and Scipio maneuvering in North Africa. Apart from being a classic on its own terms, the film is also notable for being the first film in which the long-running film character Maciste makes his debut. According to Martin Scorsese, in this work Pastrone invented the epic movie and deserves credit for many of the innovations often attributed to D.W. Griffith and Cecil B. DeMille. Among those was the extensive use of a moving camera, thus freeing the feature-length narrative film from "static gaze". The historical background and characters in the story are taken from Livy's Ab Urbe Condita (written ca. 27–25 BC). In addition, the script of Cabiria was partially based on Gustave Flaubert's 1862 novel Salammbo and Emilio Salgari's 1908 novel Cartagine in fiamme (Carthage in Flames). It was the first film shown at the White House, having been viewed on the South Lawn, by the President, First Lady, Vice President, his wife, members of the Cabinet and their wives, due to the summer heat in June 1914.

Café Paradis (English Title: Paradise Cafe) is a 1950 Danish film, directed by Bodil Ipsen and Lau Lauritzen Jr., and written by . The film received the Bodil Award for Best Danish Film, and Ib Schønberg, for what is regarded his finest performance, received the Bodil Award for Best Supporting Actor. The story illuminates the problems of alcoholism as it follows the lives of two people: one is a common workman (played by Poul Reichhardt) who drinks too much beer, and the other is a company director (played by Ib Schønberg), who believes he just needs "a little one every now and then." They both come to face the consequences of their addictions. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Paradis <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Bodil_Ipsen <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Paradis <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Lau_Lauritzen_Jr. <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Paradis <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Marie_Ejlersen <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Paradis <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Denmark <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Paradis <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Sven_Gyldmark <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Paradis <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Poul_Reichhardt <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Paradis <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Ib_Schønberg <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Paradis <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Johannes_Allen <EOT>

Cadence is a 1990 American film directed by Martin Sheen, in which Charlie Sheen plays an inmate in a United States Army military prison in West Germany during the 1960s. Sheen plays alongside his father Martin Sheen and brother Ramon Estevez. The film is based on a novel by Gordon Weaver. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadence_(film) <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Richard_Leiterman <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadence_(film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Martin_Sheen <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadence_(film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Republic_Pictures <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadence_(film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:New_Line_Cinema <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadence_(film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Georges_Delerue <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadence_(film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Frank_Giustra <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadence_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Charlie_Sheen <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadence_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Laurence_Fishburne <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadence_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Martin_Sheen <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadence_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Michael_Beach <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadence_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Ramon_Estevez <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadence_(film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Dennis_Shryack <EOT>

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabeza_de_Vaca_(film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Nicolás_Echevarría <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabeza_de_Vaca_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Juan_Diego_(actor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabeza_de_Vaca_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Daniel_Giménez_Cacho <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabeza_de_Vaca_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Roberto_Sosa_(actor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabeza_de_Vaca_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Carlos_Castañón <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabeza_de_Vaca_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Gerardo_Villarreal <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabeza_de_Vaca_(film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Álvar_Núñez_Cabeza_de_Vaca <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabeza_de_Vaca_(film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Guillermo_Sheridan <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Cabeza de Vaca is a 1991 Mexican film about the adventures of Álvar Núñez Cabeza de Vaca (c. 1490 – c. 1557), an early Spanish explorer, as he traversed what later became the American South. He was one of four survivors of the Narváez expedition and shipwreck. He became known as a shaman among the Native American tribes he encountered, which helped him survive. His journey of a number of years began in 1528. After his return to Spain, he published his journal in 1542. The screenplay by Guillermo Sheridan and Nicolás Echevarría is based on this journal. Directed by Nicolás Echevarría and starring Juan Diego, the film was entered into the 41st Berlin International Film Festival. The film was selected as the Mexican entry for the Best Foreign Language Film at the 63rd Academy Awards, but was not accepted as a nominee. A DVD version was released in 2012.

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafard <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:France <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafard <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Netherlands <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Cafard is a 2015 French-Dutch-Belgian animated war film written and directed by Jan Bultheel. The film tells the story of a boxer, Jean Mordant (based on the real-life Henri Herd, known as Constant le Marin), who joins the Belgian Expeditionary Corps which is sent to the Russian Empire during World War I in order to avenge the rape of his daughter by German soldiers in Occupied Belgium.

Cagliostro is a 1929 silent drama film directed by Richard Oswald and starring Hans Stüwe, Renée Héribel and Alfred Abel. It depicts the life of the eighteenth century Italian occultist Alessandro Cagliostro, portraying him more sympathetically than in most other works. <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caballerango <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Juan_Pablo_González <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caballerango <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Mubi_(streaming_service) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caballerango <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Isidore_Bethel <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caballerango <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Juan_Pablo_González <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Caballerango (Horse Wrangler) is a 2018 Mexican documentary film, director Juan Pablo González's debut feature. It's a portrait of residents of Milpillas in Los Altos de Jalisco as they grapple with the sudden death of a young horse wrangler named Nando. The editing alternates wide shots of landscape and community with more intimate scenes where the director, a native of the region himself, asks questions of those onscreen. Gradually, Nando's death starts to look like it might have been a suicide. It also becomes clear that the community's still reeling from the loss of several other young people. The mysterious circumstances of their demise dovetail with globalization's effects on the community: a drop in farming jobs and population exodus from the region. The film expands upon material that González's Cannes Critics' Week short, "¿Por qué el recuerdo?" ("The Solitude of Memory"), previously broached. It displays dimensions of slow cinema and includes only 37 shots across its 62-minute duration. The film's production occurred between 2013 and 2017, and it received support from the Sundance Institute, the Ford Foundation, the Austin Film Society, and the California Institute of the Arts, where González is a professor.

The screenplay was written by Harold Shumate, based on a story by Tay Garnett and Howard Higgin. Prior to filming the studio had been warned by the MPAA that the film did not comply with its code, but it is unclear whether changes were made to the script.

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_Station <PRED> dbo:imdbId <OBJ> 0051390 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_Station <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Youssef_Chahine <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_Station <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Egyptian_Arabic <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_Station <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Farid_Shawqi <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_Station <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Hind_Rostom <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Cairo Station, also called The Iron Gate (Arabic: باب الحديد Bāb al-Ḥadīd), is a 1958 Egyptian drama film directed by Youssef Chahine. It was entered for competition in the 8th Berlin International Film Festival. The film was selected as the Egyptian entry for the Best Foreign Language Film at the 31st Academy Awards, but was not accepted as a nominee. Since the 1970s, the film has found renewed interest with new generations of international film lovers and has been hailed as a masterpiece in the style of neorealist cinema. Themes depicted in the film include the urban working class, gender-based violence, and sexual repression.

Cabin in the Sky is a 1943 American musical film based on the 1940 Broadway musical of the same name. The first feature film directed by Vincente Minnelli, Cabin in the Sky features an all-black cast and stars Ethel Waters, Eddie "Rochester" Anderson and Lena Horne. Waters and Rex Ingram reprise their roles from the Broadway production as Petunia and Lucifer Junior, respectively. The film was Horne's first and only leading role in an MGM musical. Louis Armstrong is also featured in the film as one of Lucifer Junior's minions, and Duke Ellington and his Orchestra have a showcase musical number in the film. <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cahier_Africain <PRED> dbo:country <OBJ> dbr:Germany <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cahier_Africain <PRED> dbo:country <OBJ> dbr:Switzerland <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cahier_Africain <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Arabic <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cahier_Africain <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Stefan_Tolz <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Cahier Africain ([kaje afʁikɛ̃], "African Notebook") is a 2016 documentary film by Heidi Specogna, a Swiss filmmaker. Beginning in 2008, Specogna's long-term observation follows the lives of two young Central African woman, Amzine and Arlette. The film was prompted by the discovery of a small exercise book, full of courageous testimonies by more than 300 victims of war crimes committed by Central African mercenaries during armed conflict between October 2002 and March 2003.

Calais-Dover (French: Calais-Douvres) is a 1931 French-German comedy film directed by Jean Boyer and Anatole Litvak and starring Lilian Harvey, André Roanne and Armand Bernard. It is the French-language version of the German film No More Love, with Harvey reprising her role. The title refers to the Dover–Calais ferry. It incorporated location shooting on the French Riviera with interiors shot at the Babelsberg Studios in Berlin. The film's sets were designed by the art directors Robert Herlth, Walter Röhrig and Werner Schlichting. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calais-Dover_(film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:L'Alliance_Cinématographique_Européenne <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calais-Dover_(film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Aleksandr_Uralsky <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calais-Dover_(film) <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:French_language <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calais-Dover_(film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Mischa_Spoliansky <EOT>
Cafe Moscow (Hungarian:Café Moszkva) is a 1936 Hungarian adventure film directed by Steve Sekely and starring Anna Tõkés, Gyula Csortos and Ferenc Kiss. Art direction was by . It is also known by the alternative title Only One Night. The film is set during the First World War on the Eastern Front between Russia and the Austro-Hungarian Empire. The film was intended to convey an anti-war message. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Moscow <PRED> dbo:releaseDate <OBJ> 1936-02-13 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Moscow <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Rudolf_Icsey <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Moscow <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Willy_Goldberger <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Moscow <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Steve_Sekely <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Moscow <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Ladislao_Vajda <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Moscow <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Hungarian_language <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Moscow <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Alexander_Laszlo_(composer) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Moscow <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Steve_Sekely <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Moscow <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:István_Tamás <EOT>

The film is produced by Sayed Zulfikar Abbas Bukhari (Zulfi Bukhari) and is a joint production by Asim Abbasi's United Kingdom-based production company Indus Talkies, and a Pakistani film production company ZAB Films. The film stars Sanam Saeed and Aamina Sheikh as lead characters alongside Adnan Malik in his film debut. A five-part prologue webisodes short-series was also released on YouTube, focusing on the lives of Zara and Adnan in London. It was selected as the Pakistani entry for the Best Foreign Language Film at the 91st Academy Awards, but it was not nominated.

Cafundó is 2005 Brazilian historical drama film written and directed by Paulo Betti and Clóvis Bueno and starring Lázaro Ramos. The film is a biopic based on miracle worker preto velho João de Camargo of Sorocaba and is based on the book João de Camargo de Sorocaba: O Nascimento de uma Religião by Carlos de Campos and Adolfo Frioli. The title comes from a former quilombo, the source of João de Camargo's original spiritual inspiration, located in today's Salto de Pirapora. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafundó_(film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Paulo_Betti <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafundó_(film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:André_Abujamra <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafundó_(film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Paulo_Betti <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafundó_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Leona_Cavalli <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafundó_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Lázaro_Ramos <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafundó_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Leandro_Firmino_da_Hora <EOT>

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadets_(film) <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Günther_Anders_(cinematographer) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadets_(film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Karl_Ritter_(director) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadets_(film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Universum_Film_AG <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadets_(film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Gottfried_Ritter <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadets_(film) <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:German_language <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadets_(film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Herbert_Windt <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadets_(film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Karl_Ritter_(director) <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Cadets (German: Kadetten) is a 1939 German historical war film directed by Karl Ritter and starring Mathias Wieman, Carsta Löck, and Andrews Engelmann. The film is set in 1760, against the backdrop of the Austro-Russian Raid on Berlin during the Seven Years' War. It depicts a group of Prussian cadets holding off superior Russian forces. Because of its anti-Russian theme the film was pulled from release in 1939 following the Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact. It was put on general release in December 1941, once Germany and the Soviets were at war. The film is loosely connected to the Prussian film cycle of historical epics.

Cairo Declaration is a 2015 Chinese 2D historical film directed by and and written by Liu Xing. The film stars Hu Jun, Cecilia Han, Ma Xiaowei, and Tang Guoqiang. The film was scheduled to be released on September 3, 2015. Cabin Fever is a 2016 American science fiction horror film directed by Travis Zariwny (under the pseudonym Travis Z) and written by Eli Roth. A remake of Roth's 2002 film of the same name and the fourth installment in the Cabin Fever series, the film stars Samuel Davis, Gage Golightly, Matthew Daddario, Nadine Crocker, and Dustin Ingram. The film was released on February 12, 2016, by IFC Midnight. Eli Roth, writer and director of the original film, acts as co-writer and executive producer. The film was poorly received by critics and underperformed at the box office. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:IFC_Midnight <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Kevin_Riepl <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Matthew_Daddario <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Gage_Golightly <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Dustin_Ingram <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Eli_Roth <EOT>

Café de Flore is a Canadian drama film, released in 2011. Directed, written, and edited by Jean-Marc Vallée, the film garnered 13 nominations for the 2012 Genie Awards. The film's title refers not to the café on Boulevard Saint-Germain in Paris, but to a Matthew Herbert song of the same name which the film uses to represent its musical current. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_de_Flore_(film) <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Pierre_Cottereau <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_de_Flore_(film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Jean-Marc_Vallée <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_de_Flore_(film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Alliance_Films <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_de_Flore_(film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Jean-Marc_Vallée <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_de_Flore_(film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Pierre_Even_(producer) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_de_Flore_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Vanessa_Paradis <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_de_Flore_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Evelyne_Brochu <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_de_Flore_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Hélène_Florent <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_de_Flore_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Kevin_Parent <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_de_Flore_(film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Jean-Marc_Vallée <EOT>
