<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadillac_Records <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Darnell_Martin <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadillac_Records <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Sony_Pictures_Releasing <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadillac_Records <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Darnell_Martin <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Cadillac Records is a 2008 American biographical drama film written and directed by Darnell Martin. The film explores the musical era from the early 1940s to the late 1960s, chronicling the life of the influential Chicago-based record-company executive Leonard Chess, and a few of the musicians who recorded for Chess Records. The film stars Adrien Brody as Leonard Chess, Cedric the Entertainer as Willie Dixon, Mos Def as Chuck Berry, Columbus Short as Little Walter, Jeffrey Wright as Muddy Waters, Eamonn Walker as Howlin' Wolf, and Beyoncé Knowles as Etta James. The film was released in North America on December 5, 2008, by TriStar Pictures. The soundtrack was released on Music World/Columbia and Sony Music.

Cadets (German: Kadetten) is a 1939 German historical war film directed by Karl Ritter and starring Mathias Wieman, Carsta Löck, and Andrews Engelmann. The film is set in 1760, against the backdrop of the Austro-Russian Raid on Berlin during the Seven Years' War. It depicts a group of Prussian cadets holding off superior Russian forces. Because of its anti-Russian theme the film was pulled from release in 1939 following the Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact. It was put on general release in December 1941, once Germany and the Soviets were at war. The film is loosely connected to the Prussian film cycle of historical epics. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadets_(film) <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Günther_Anders_(cinematographer) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadets_(film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Karl_Ritter_(director) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadets_(film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Universum_Film_AG <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadets_(film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Gottfried_Ritter <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadets_(film) <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:German_language <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadets_(film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Herbert_Windt <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadets_(film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Karl_Ritter_(director) <EOT>
Caffè Italia, Montréal is a Canadian docudrama film, directed by Paul Tana and released in 1985. Focusing on the Italian Canadian community in Montreal, Quebec, the film profiles the community's history through a mix of archival footage and historical reenactments of key events acted by a cast led by Pierre Curzi and Tony Nardi. The film won the Prix L.-E.-Ouimet-Molson from the Association québécoise des critiques de cinéma for 1985. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caffè_Italia,_Montréal <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Paul_Tana <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caffè_Italia,_Montréal <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Tony_Nardi <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caffè_Italia,_Montréal <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Pierre_Curzi <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caffè_Italia,_Montréal <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Paul_Tana <EOT>

Cadaver is a 2022 Indian Tamil-language police procedural thriller film directed by Anoop Panicker and written by Abhilash Pillai. The film was under Production House Amala Paul Productions. The film stars Amala Paul with Riythvika, Munishkanth, Thrigun, Harish Uthaman and Athulya Ravi in supporting roles. Caddyshack II is a 1988 American sports comedy film and a sequel to the 1980 film Caddyshack. Directed by Allan Arkush and written by Harold Ramis (who co-wrote and directed the original Caddyshack) and PJ Torokvei, it stars Jackie Mason, Robert Stack, Dyan Cannon, Dina Merrill, Jonathan Silverman, Brian McNamara, Marsha Warfield, Paul Bartel, and Randy Quaid with special appearances by Chevy Chase and Dan Aykroyd. While the writing of the film is officially credited to Ramis and Torokvei, the first-draft script by Ramis and Torokvei was rewritten by other uncredited writers. The sequel was panned by critics and is considered one of the worst sequels of all time. However, Kenny Loggins' "Nobody's Fool" which was used as the film's theme song was a chart success where it hit #8 on the Billboard Hot 100. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Harry_Stradling_Jr. <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Allan_Arkush <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Warner_Bros. <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Bernard_Gribble <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Ira_Newborn <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Jon_Peters <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Peter_Guber <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Neil_Canton <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Robert_Stack <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jonathan_Silverman <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Paul_Bartel <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Dan_Aykroyd <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Dyan_Cannon <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Brian_McNamara <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jackie_Mason <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Chevy_Chase <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Dina_Merrill <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Marsha_Warfield <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Randy_Quaid <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:PJ_Torokvei <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack_II <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Harold_Ramis <EOT>

Cadillac Man is a 1990 American black comedy film directed by Roger Donaldson, starring Robin Williams and Tim Robbins. The plot of the film centers on car salesman Joey O'Brien (Williams) whose life is consumed by turmoil, which all comes to a head when his dealership is taken hostage by Larry (Robbins), a crazed motorcyclist. Cabaret is a 1972 American musical drama film directed by Bob Fosse, and starring Liza Minnelli, Michael York and Joel Grey. Set in Berlin during the Weimar Republic in 1931, under the presence of the growing Nazi Party, the film is loosely based on the 1966 Broadway musical Cabaret by Kander and Ebb, which was adapted from Christopher Isherwood's semi-autobiographical novel The Berlin Stories (1945) as well as John Van Druten's 1951 play I Am a Camera, which was itself adapted from Isherwood's novel. Multiple numbers from the stage score were used for the film, which also featured three other songs by Kander and Ebb, including two written for the adaptation. In the traditional manner of musical theater, most major characters in the stage version sing to express their emotions and advance the plot; in the film, however, the musical numbers are entirely diegetic. All of them take place inside the club, with one exception: "Tomorrow Belongs to Me", the only song sung by neither the Master of Ceremonies nor Sally Bowles. After the box-office failure of his 1969 film version of Sweet Charity, Fosse bounced back with Cabaret in 1972, a year that made him one of the most honored working directors in Hollywood. The film also brought Minnelli, daughter of Judy Garland and Vincente Minnelli, her own first chance to sing on screen, and she won the Academy Award for Best Actress. With Academy Awards for Best Supporting Actor (Grey), Best Director (Fosse), Best Cinematography, Best Art Direction, Best Sound, Best Original Song Score and Adaptation, and Best Film Editing, Cabaret holds the record for most Oscars earned by a film not honored for Best Picture. It is listed as number 367 on Empire's 500 greatest films of all time. Cabaret opened to glowing reviews and strong box office, eventually taking in more than $40 million. In addition to its eight Oscars, it won Best Picture citations from the National Board of Review and the Hollywood Foreign Press Association, and took Best Supporting Actor honors for Grey from the National Board of Review, the Hollywood Foreign Press, and the National Society of Film Critics. In 1995, Cabaret was the twelfth live-action musical film selected by the Library of Congress for preservation in the United States National Film Registry as being deemed "culturally, historically, or aesthetically significant". <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Geoffrey_Unsworth <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Bob_Fosse <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:20th_Century_Fox <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:David_Bretherton <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Fred_Ebb <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:John_Kander <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Ralph_Burns <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Cy_Feuer <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Fritz_Wepper <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Liza_Minnelli <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Helmut_Griem <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Joel_Grey <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Marisa_Berenson <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Michael_York <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Jay_Presson_Allen <EOT>

Caged Heat, also known as Renegade Girls, is a 1974 women in prison film. It was written and directed by Jonathan Demme (in his directorial debut) for New World Pictures, headed by Roger Corman. The film stars Juanita Brown, Roberta Collins, Erica Gavin, Ella Reid, Rainbeaux Smith, and Barbara Steele. John Cale wrote and performed its soundtrack music, which features the guitar playing of Mike Bloomfield. Two later films, Caged Heat II: Stripped of Freedom (1994) and Caged Heat 3000 (1995), made use of the Caged Heat name and the women-in-prison situation, but are unrelated to the original film. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Tak_Fujimoto <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Jonathan_Demme <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:New_World_Communications <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:John_Cale <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Roger_Corman <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Roberta_Collins <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Barbara_Steele <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Erica_Gavin <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Rainbeaux_Smith <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Jonathan_Demme <EOT>

Cabin Fever 2: Spring Fever (also known as Cabin Fever 2 or Cabin Fever: Spring Fever) is a 2009 American horror comedy film directed by Ti West and stars Noah Segan, Rusty Kelley, Alexi Wasser, Marc Senter, Rider Strong and Giuseppe Andrews. It is a sequel to the 2002 film Cabin Fever and the second installment in the Cabin Fever series. The film's title refers not to the café on Boulevard Saint-Germain in Paris, but to a Matthew Herbert song of the same name which the film uses to represent its musical current.

Caged is a 1950 American women-in-prison film noir directed by John Cromwell and starring Eleanor Parker, Agnes Moorehead, Betty Garde, Hope Emerson, and Ellen Corby. It was nominated for three Academy Awards. The film portrays the story of a young newlywed sent to prison for armed robbery. Her brutal experiences while incarcerated, along with the killing of her husband, transform her from a meek, naive woman into a hardened convict. The film's subplot includes massive prison corruption. Caged was adapted by Virginia Kellogg from the story "Women Without Men" by Kellogg and Bernard C. Schoenfeld. The studio had originally intended the film to be a vehicle for Bette Davis and Joan Crawford, but reportedly Davis had said she did not want to make a "dyke movie" (a film with lesbian content) and turned it down. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:imdbId <OBJ> 0042296 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Carl_E._Guthrie <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:John_Cromwell_(director) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Warner_Bros. <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Owen_Marks <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Max_Steiner <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Jerry_Wald <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Betty_Garde <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Hope_Emerson <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Eleanor_Parker <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Ellen_Corby <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Agnes_Moorehead <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Bernard_C._Schoenfeld <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Virginia_Kellogg <EOT>

Cahier Africain ([kaje afʁikɛ̃], "African Notebook") is a 2016 documentary film by Heidi Specogna, a Swiss filmmaker. Beginning in 2008, Specogna's long-term observation follows the lives of two young Central African woman, Amzine and Arlette. The film was prompted by the discovery of a small exercise book, full of courageous testimonies by more than 300 victims of war crimes committed by Central African mercenaries during armed conflict between October 2002 and March 2003. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cahier_Africain <PRED> dbo:country <OBJ> dbr:Germany <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cahier_Africain <PRED> dbo:country <OBJ> dbr:Switzerland <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cahier_Africain <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Arabic <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cahier_Africain <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Stefan_Tolz <EOT>

Cabaret is a 2019 Indian romantic drama thriller dance film directed by Kaustav Narayan Niyogi, produced by Pooja Bhatt and Bhushan Kumar under the banner of Fisheye Network private limited. Principal photography of the film began around 9 June 2015. Originally scheduled for a 2016 release, alleged copyright violations led to delays before its eventual release on 9 January 2019. <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_in_the_Sky_(film) <PRED> dbo:country <OBJ> dbr:United_States <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_in_the_Sky_(film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Vincente_Minnelli <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_in_the_Sky_(film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Busby_Berkeley <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_in_the_Sky_(film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Loews_Cineplex_Entertainment <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_in_the_Sky_(film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Harold_F._Kress <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_in_the_Sky_(film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:George_Bassman <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_in_the_Sky_(film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Georgie_Stoll <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_in_the_Sky_(film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Hall_Johnson <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_in_the_Sky_(film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Roger_Edens <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_in_the_Sky_(film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Albert_Lewis_(producer) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_in_the_Sky_(film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Arthur_Freed <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_in_the_Sky_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Rex_Ingram_(actor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_in_the_Sky_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Lena_Horne <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_in_the_Sky_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Louis_Armstrong <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_in_the_Sky_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Eddie_%22Rochester%22_Anderson <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_in_the_Sky_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Ethel_Waters <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_in_the_Sky_(film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Marc_Connelly <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Cabin in the Sky is a 1943 American musical film based on the 1940 Broadway musical of the same name. The first feature film directed by Vincente Minnelli, Cabin in the Sky features an all-black cast and stars Ethel Waters, Eddie "Rochester" Anderson and Lena Horne. Waters and Rex Ingram reprise their roles from the Broadway production as Petunia and Lucifer Junior, respectively. The film was Horne's first and only leading role in an MGM musical. Louis Armstrong is also featured in the film as one of Lucifer Junior's minions, and Duke Ellington and his Orchestra have a showcase musical number in the film. In 2020, the film was selected for preservation in the United States National Film Registry by the Library of Congress as being "culturally, historically, or aesthetically significant".

Cadillac Records is a 2008 American biographical drama film written and directed by Darnell Martin. The film explores the musical era from the early 1940s to the late 1960s, chronicling the life of the influential Chicago-based record-company executive Leonard Chess, and a few of the musicians who recorded for Chess Records. The film stars Adrien Brody as Leonard Chess, Cedric the Entertainer as Willie Dixon, Mos Def as Chuck Berry, Columbus Short as Little Walter, Jeffrey Wright as Muddy Waters, Eamonn Walker as Howlin' Wolf, and Beyoncé Knowles as Etta James. The film was released in North America on December 5, 2008, by TriStar Pictures. The soundtrack was released on Music World/Columbia and Sony Music. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadillac_Records <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Darnell_Martin <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadillac_Records <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Sony_Pictures_Releasing <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cadillac_Records <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Darnell_Martin <EOT>

Cactus Flower is a 1969 American screwball comedy film directed by Gene Saks and starring Walter Matthau, Ingrid Bergman, and Goldie Hawn, who won an Academy Award for her performance. Along with Hello Dolly!, are the movies that end the Golden Age of Hollywood.[citation?] The screenplay was adapted by I. A. L. Diamond from the 1965 Broadway play of the same name written by Abe Burrows, which in turn was based upon the French play Fleur de cactus by Pierre Barillet and Jean-Pierre Gredy. <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Cristian_Nemescu <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:IFC_Films <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Romanian_Armed_Forces <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:English_language <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Cristian_Nemescu <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Răzvan_Vasilescu <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jamie_Elman <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Armand_Assante <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Maria_Dinulescu <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Cristian_Nemescu <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Catherine_Linstrum <EOT> <RDF2Text>	California Dreamin' (endless) (Romanian: California Dreamin' (nesfârșit)) is a 2007 Romanian film by Cristian Nemescu. It won the Prix un certain regard at the 2007 Cannes Film Festival. It also picked up the Iris Award for Best Film, the Audience Award and the Canvas Award at the Brussels European Film Festival 2007. The film is also sometimes called Endless in English, nesfârșit being Romanian for "endless". The director died before editing was completed. MediaPro Studios decided to edit the film with the entirety of the material left by Nemescu, a decision which led to the considerable runtime of 155 minutes.

Ca-bau-kan (Chinese: 擦包看), also known as The Courtesan, is a 2002 Indonesian romantic drama film, directed by Nia Dinata, and starring Niniek L. Karim, and . It was distributed by and released on February 7, 2002 in Jakarta. Cabin Fever: Patient Zero is a 2014 science fiction horror film directed by Kaare Andrews and written by Jake Wade Wall. Starring Ryan Donowho, Brando Eaton, Jillian Murray, Mitch Ryan, Lydia Hearst and Sean Astin. <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Nigel_Cole <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Walt_Disney_Studios_Motion_Pictures <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Patrick_Doyle <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Julie_Walters <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Penelope_Wilton <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Annette_Crosbie <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Linda_Bassett <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Celia_Imrie <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Harriet_Thorpe <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Helen_Mirren <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girls <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Tim_Firth <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Calendar Girls is a 2003 British comedy film directed by Nigel Cole. Produced by Touchstone Pictures, it features a screenplay by Tim Firth and Juliette Towhidi, based on a true story of a group of middle-aged Yorkshire women who produced a nude calendar to raise money for Leukaemia Research under the auspices of the Women's Institutes in April 1999 after the husband of one of their members dies from cancer. The film stars an ensemble cast headed by Helen Mirren and Julie Walters, with Linda Bassett, Annette Crosbie, Celia Imrie, Penelope Wilton, Geraldine James, Harriet Thorpe and Philip Glenister playing key supporting roles. Calendar Girls premiered at the Locarno Film Festival and was later shown at Filmfest Hamburg, the Dinard Festival of British Cinema in France, the Warsaw Film Festival, the Tokyo International Film Festival and the UK Film Festival in Hong Kong. It garnered generally positive reactions by film critics, who compared it with another British comedy film The Full Monty (1997). At a budget of $10 million it also became a major commercial success, eventually grossing $93.4 million worldwide following its theatrical release in the U.S. In addition, the picture was awarded the British Comedy Award for Best Comedy Film, and received ALFS Award, Empire Award and Satellite Award nominations for Mirren and Walters, and a Golden Globe Award nomination for Mirren.

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Tak_Fujimoto <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Jonathan_Demme <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:New_World_Communications <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:John_Cale <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Roger_Corman <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Roberta_Collins <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Barbara_Steele <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Erica_Gavin <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Rainbeaux_Smith <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_Heat <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Jonathan_Demme <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Caged Heat, also known as Renegade Girls, is a 1974 women in prison film. It was written and directed by Jonathan Demme (in his directorial debut) for New World Pictures, headed by Roger Corman. The film stars Juanita Brown, Roberta Collins, Erica Gavin, Ella Reid, Rainbeaux Smith, and Barbara Steele. John Cale wrote and performed its soundtrack music, which features the guitar playing of Mike Bloomfield. Two later films, Caged Heat II: Stripped of Freedom (1994) and Caged Heat 3000 (1995), made use of the Caged Heat name and the women-in-prison situation, but are unrelated to the original film.

Cabaret Paradis (Cabaret Paradise) is a 2006 French comedy film. The plot revolves around Shirley and Dino (Corinne and Gilles Benizio respectively), two entertainers as they purchase an old cabaret, in Paris, which they desperately try to put back on its feet. <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Stevan_Larner <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Harold_Ramis <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Warner_Bros. <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Johnny_Mandel <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Douglas_Kenney <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Rodney_Dangerfield <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Bill_Murray <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Ted_Knight <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Chevy_Chase <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Michael_O'Keefe <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Brian_Doyle-Murray <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Harold_Ramis <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caddyshack <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Douglas_Kenney <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Caddyshack is a 1980 American sports comedy film directed by Harold Ramis, written by Brian Doyle-Murray, Ramis and Douglas Kenney, and starring Chevy Chase, Rodney Dangerfield, Ted Knight, Michael O'Keefe and Bill Murray with supporting roles by Sarah Holcomb, Cindy Morgan, and Doyle-Murray. Caddyshack was Ramis's directorial debut and boosted the career of Dangerfield, who was previously known mostly for his stand-up comedy. Grossing nearly $40 million at the domestic box office (the 17th-highest of the year), it was the first of a series of similar comedies. The film has a cult following and was described by ESPN as "perhaps the funniest sports movie ever made." A sequel, Caddyshack II (1988), followed, although only Chase reprised his role and the film was poorly received.

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caine's_Arcade <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Nirvan_Mullick <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Caine's Arcade is an 11-minute short documentary film by Nirvan Mullick released on April 9, 2012 that features a cardboard arcade created by then 9-year-old Caine Monroy out of boxes and everyday objects. The boy ran his arcade from his father's auto parts store in East Los Angeles mid-2011. Nirvan was inspired to make the documentary after unexpectedly coming across the arcade while getting a door handle for his car. Nirvan became Caine's first customer, purchasing a $2 Fun Pass, and decided to make a film about Caine's Arcade after witnessing the level of commitment, work, and thought Caine had put into the arcade. After learning he had been Caine's first and only customer, Nirvan used social media to arrange a surprise flash mob of customers to come to play Caine's Arcade, which was included in the film. After being uploaded on YouTube, the short film soon became a viral video, and numerous people donated money towards a college fund that Nirvan had established for Caine. Since the film's release, schools around the world have recreated similar cardboard arcades, and the positive response inspired Nirvan and the team to start the Imagination Foundation, a non-profit aimed at fostering creativity and entrepreneurship in adults across the world.

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Geoffrey_Unsworth <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Bob_Fosse <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:20th_Century_Fox <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:David_Bretherton <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Fred_Ebb <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:John_Kander <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Ralph_Burns <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Cy_Feuer <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Fritz_Wepper <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Liza_Minnelli <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Helmut_Griem <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Joel_Grey <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Marisa_Berenson <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Michael_York <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabaret_(1972_film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Jay_Presson_Allen <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Cabaret is a 1972 American musical drama film directed by Bob Fosse, and starring Liza Minnelli, Michael York and Joel Grey. Set in Berlin during the Weimar Republic in 1931, under the presence of the growing Nazi Party, the film is loosely based on the 1966 Broadway musical Cabaret by Kander and Ebb, which was adapted from Christopher Isherwood's semi-autobiographical novel The Berlin Stories (1945) as well as John Van Druten's 1951 play I Am a Camera, which was itself adapted from Isherwood's novel. Multiple numbers from the stage score were used for the film, which also featured three other songs by Kander and Ebb, including two written for the adaptation. In the traditional manner of musical theater, most major characters in the stage version sing to express their emotions and advance the plot; in the film, however, the musical numbers are entirely diegetic. All of them take place inside the club, with one exception: "Tomorrow Belongs to Me", the only song sung by neither the Master of Ceremonies nor Sally Bowles. After the box-office failure of his 1969 film version of Sweet Charity, Fosse bounced back with Cabaret in 1972, a year that made him one of the most honored working directors in Hollywood. The film also brought Minnelli, daughter of Judy Garland and Vincente Minnelli, her own first chance to sing on screen, and she won the Academy Award for Best Actress. With Academy Awards for Best Supporting Actor (Grey), Best Director (Fosse), Best Cinematography, Best Art Direction, Best Sound, Best Original Song Score and Adaptation, and Best Film Editing, Cabaret holds the record for most Oscars earned by a film not honored for Best Picture. It is listed as number 367 on Empire's 500 greatest films of all time. Cabaret opened to glowing reviews and strong box office, eventually taking in more than $40 million. In addition to its eight Oscars, it won Best Picture citations from the National Board of Review and the Hollywood Foreign Press Association, and took Best Supporting Actor honors for Grey from the National Board of Review, the Hollywood Foreign Press, and the National Society of Film Critics. In 1995, Cabaret was the twelfth live-action musical film selected by the Library of Congress for preservation in the United States National Film Registry as being deemed "culturally, historically, or aesthetically significant".

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caesar_and_Otto's_Deadly_Xmas <PRED> <MASK> <OBJ> dbr:Joe_Estevez <EOT>	dbo:starring
Cabin Fever is a 2002 American horror comedy film co-written and directed by Eli Roth (in his directorial debut) and starring Rider Strong, Jordan Ladd, James DeBello, Cerina Vincent, Joey Kern, and Giuseppe Andrews. The story follows a group of college graduates who rent a cabin in the woods and begin to fall victim to a flesh-eating virus. The inspiration for the film's story came from a real-life experience during a trip to Iceland when Roth developed a skin infection. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2002_film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Eli_Roth <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2002_film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Lionsgate_Films <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2002_film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Nathan_Barr <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2002_film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Eli_Roth <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2002_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Rider_Strong <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2002_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Giuseppe_Andrews <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2002_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Cerina_Vincent <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2002_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jordan_Ladd <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2002_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Arie_Verveen <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2002_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Joey_Kern <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabin_Fever_(2002_film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Eli_Roth <EOT>

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Abel_(1982_film) <PRED> dbo:country <OBJ> dbr:Philippines <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Abel_(1982_film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Lino_Brocka <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Abel_(1982_film) <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:English_language <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Abel_(1982_film) <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Filipino_language <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Abel_(1982_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Carmi_Martin <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Abel_(1982_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Christopher_de_Leon <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Abel_(1982_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Mona_Lisa_(actress) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Abel_(1982_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Phillip_Salvador <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cain_and_Abel_(1982_film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Ricky_Lee <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Cain and Abel (Filipino: Cain at Abel) is a 1982 Philippine action thriller drama film directed by Lino Brocka from a written story and screenplay by Ricardo "Ricky" Lee. The film's story was inspired by the Biblical story of two brothers, Christopher de Leon and Phillip Salvador respectively played the roles of Ellis and Lorenzo, the two brothers and sons of Senyora Pina (Mona Lisa), who have different views on each other. However, the sibling rivalry became violent and bloody due to the issue of inheritance of their family land and Senyora Pina's favoritism to her younger son. It also stars Carmi Martin as Zita, Ellis's fiancée from Manila; Cecille Castillo as Rina, the house helper, and Ellis's other woman; and Baby Delgado as Becky, Lorenzo's wife. Cain at Abel was released on October 8, 1982, by Cine Suerte Inc., it served as the first Filipino film entry for the San Sebastián International Film Festival in Spain in the same year, and received accolades from award-giving bodies for cinema. The film was digitally restored and remastered by ABS-CBN Film Restoration Project and Central Digital Lab in 2016; the restored version was premiered on August 11, 2016.

After a debut at the Edinburgh International Film Festival, it was released on 29 June 2018 on Netflix. It also had a limited release in select Curzon Cinemas in the UK from 21 October to 16 November 2018. The film is set in Scotland and concerns incidents on a hunting trip to the remote Scottish Highlands, and stars Jack Lowden and Martin McCann.

Calcutta 71 is a 1972 Bengali film directed by noted Indian art film director Mrinal Sen. This film is considered to be the second film of Mrinal Sen's Calcutta trilogy, the others being Interview, and Padatik. The movie Calcutta 71 is a collection of stories depicting the Seventies. The Naxalite activity, starvation of common people, social and political corruption are shown. Caliber 9 (Italian: Milano calibro 9, lit. 'Milan caliber 9'; also released as The Contract) is a 1972 Italian noir-poliziottesco film written and directed by Fernando Di Leo and starring Gastone Moschin, Mario Adorf, Barbara Bouchet, Philippe Leroy, Frank Wolff, Luigi Pistilli, and Lionel Stander. The film takes its title from the short story collection of the same name by Giorgio Scerbanenco, and is partially based on three of its stories. The musical score was composed by Luis Enriquez Bacalov and performed by the progressive rock band Osanna. Caliber 9 is the first part in Di Leo's Milieu Trilogy of poliziotteschi films. It was followed by La mala ordina (The Italian Connection) in 1972 and Il Boss (The Boss) in 1973. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caliber_9 <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Fernando_Di_Leo <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caliber_9 <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Osanna <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caliber_9 <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Luis_Enríquez_Bacalov <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caliber_9 <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Frank_Wolff_(actor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caliber_9 <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Gastone_Moschin <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caliber_9 <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Lionel_Stander <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caliber_9 <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Luigi_Pistilli <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caliber_9 <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Barbara_Bouchet <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caliber_9 <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Ivo_Garrani <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caliber_9 <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Mario_Adorf <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caliber_9 <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Philippe_Leroy_(actor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caliber_9 <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Fernando_Di_Leo <EOT>

Calendar Girl is a 1993 American comedy-drama film starring Jason Priestley, Gabriel Olds, and Jerry O'Connell. The film was directed by John Whitesell and written by Paul W. Shapiro. Set in 1962, it tells the story of three young men who go on a trip to Hollywood to fulfil their dream of meeting Marilyn Monroe. It has similarities to the real-life story of Gene Scanlon, who in 1953 crossed America with a friend and had a date with Marilyn Monroe for which she paid the bill. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girl_(1993_film) <PRED> dbo:imdbId <OBJ> 0106505 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girl_(1993_film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:John_Whitesell <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girl_(1993_film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Columbia_Pictures <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girl_(1993_film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Wendy_Greene_Bricmont <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girl_(1993_film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Hans_Zimmer <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girl_(1993_film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Penny_Marshall <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girl_(1993_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jason_Priestley <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girl_(1993_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Joe_Pantoliano <EOT>

Cake is a 2018 Pakistani comedy drama film which is directed by Asim Abbasi. The film is produced by Sayed Zulfikar Abbas Bukhari (Zulfi Bukhari) and is a joint production by Asim Abbasi's United Kingdom-based production company Indus Talkies, and a Pakistani film production company ZAB Films. The film stars Sanam Saeed and Aamina Sheikh as lead characters alongside Adnan Malik in his film debut. A five-part prologue webisodes short-series was also released on YouTube, focusing on the lives of Zara and Adnan in London. It was selected as the Pakistani entry for the Best Foreign Language Film at the 91st Academy Awards, but it was not nominated. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cake_(2018_film) <PRED> dbo:country <OBJ> dbr:United_Kingdom <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cake_(2018_film) <PRED> dbo:country <OBJ> dbr:Pakistan <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cake_(2018_film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Asim_Abbasi <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cake_(2018_film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Aarti_Bajaj <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cake_(2018_film) <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Urdu <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cake_(2018_film) <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Sindhi_language <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cake_(2018_film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:The_Sketches <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cake_(2018_film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Sayed_Zulfiqar_Abbas_Bukhari <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cake_(2018_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Sanam_Saeed <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cake_(2018_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Aamina_Sheikh <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cake_(2018_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Adnan_Malik <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cake_(2018_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Syed_Mohammad_Ahmed <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cake_(2018_film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Asim_Abbasi <EOT>

Cabin by the Lake is a horror TV movie released in 2000. It tells the story of Stanley, played by Judd Nelson, a script writer who begins killing girls for research for a movie he is writing, where the villain does the same thing. California Dreamin' (endless) (Romanian: California Dreamin' (nesfârșit)) is a 2007 Romanian film by Cristian Nemescu. It won the Prix un certain regard at the 2007 Cannes Film Festival. It also picked up the Iris Award for Best Film, the Audience Award and the Canvas Award at the Brussels European Film Festival 2007. The film is also sometimes called Endless in English, nesfârșit being Romanian for "endless". The director died before editing was completed. MediaPro Studios decided to edit the film with the entirety of the material left by Nemescu, a decision which led to the considerable runtime of 155 minutes. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Cristian_Nemescu <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:IFC_Films <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Romanian_Armed_Forces <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:English_language <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Cristian_Nemescu <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Răzvan_Vasilescu <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jamie_Elman <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Armand_Assante <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Maria_Dinulescu <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Cristian_Nemescu <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Dreamin'_(film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Catherine_Linstrum <EOT>

Calapor is a 2013 Bollywood thriller film produced by and by directed by . The film is a taut thriller, set in the backdrop of a jail. It is a modern story of reformation. The film provokes thoughts about the nature of human being while infusing hope that there is good in every human being. The film is slated for 2 August 2013 release. <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girl_(1993_film) <PRED> dbo:imdbId <OBJ> 0106505 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girl_(1993_film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:John_Whitesell <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girl_(1993_film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Columbia_Pictures <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girl_(1993_film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Wendy_Greene_Bricmont <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girl_(1993_film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Hans_Zimmer <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girl_(1993_film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Penny_Marshall <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girl_(1993_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jason_Priestley <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calendar_Girl_(1993_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Joe_Pantoliano <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Calendar Girl is a 1993 American comedy-drama film starring Jason Priestley, Gabriel Olds, and Jerry O'Connell. The film was directed by John Whitesell and written by Paul W. Shapiro. Set in 1962, it tells the story of three young men who go on a trip to Hollywood to fulfil their dream of meeting Marilyn Monroe. It has similarities to the real-life story of Gene Scanlon, who in 1953 crossed America with a friend and had a date with Marilyn Monroe for which she paid the bill.

Calaboose is a 1943 American Western film directed by Hal Roach Jr. It stars Jimmy Rogers, Mary Brian and Noah Beery Jr. It is a sequel to Dudes are Pretty People (1942), a featurette from "Hal Roach's Streamliners" which is a series of approximately 50-minute comedic movies. The film runs 45 minutes. Another sequel followed later the same year, with Rogers and Beery playing the same characters, entitled Prairie Chickens. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calaboose_(film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Hal_Roach_Jr. <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calaboose_(film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:United_Artists <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calaboose_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Noah_Beery_Jr. <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calaboose_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jimmy_Rogers_(actor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calaboose_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Mary_Brian <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Calaboose_(film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Donald_Hough <EOT>

The story follows a group of college graduates who rent a cabin in the woods and begin to fall victim to a flesh-eating virus. The inspiration for the film's story came from a real-life experience during a trip to Iceland when Roth developed a skin infection.

Caballo prieto azabache (La tumba de Villa) is a 1968 Mexican historical drama film starring Antonio Aguilar, Flor Silvestre, and Jaime Fernández. It focuses on a horse breeder named Jesús who is set on buying a horse known as "Caballo prieto" (dark horse) and pursuing a relationship with a singer named Genoveva Alarios. With he and Genoveva eventually recruited as spies for the revolutionary leader Pancho Villa. The film was successful at the box-office and stayed in theaters for a surprising nine weeks. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caballo_prieto_azabache_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jaime_Fernández_(actor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caballo_prieto_azabache_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Antonio_Aguilar <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caballo_prieto_azabache_(film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Flor_Silvestre <EOT>

Café Society is a 2016 American romantic comedy-drama film written and directed by Woody Allen. It stars Jesse Eisenberg, Kristen Stewart, Steve Carell, Jeannie Berlin, Blake Lively, Parker Posey, Corey Stoll, and Ken Stott. The plot follows a young man who moves to Hollywood in the 1930s, where he falls in love with the assistant to his uncle, a powerful talent agent. The film had its premiere at the Cannes Film Festival on May 11, 2016, and was theatrically released in the United States on July 15, 2016, by Amazon Studios and Lionsgate. It received generally positive reviews and grossed $43 million. It received nomination at the Golden Eagle Award in 2017 for Best Foreign Language Film. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Society_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Vittorio_Storaro <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Society_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Woody_Allen <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Society_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Lionsgate_Films <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Society_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Amazon_Studios <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Society_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Alisa_Lepselter <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Society_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Blake_Lively <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Society_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Corey_Stoll <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Society_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Steve_Carell <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Society_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Parker_Posey <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Society_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jeannie_Berlin <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Society_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jesse_Eisenberg <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Society_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Ken_Stott <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Society_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Kristen_Stewart <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Café_Society_(2016_film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Woody_Allen <EOT>

Some scenes were directed by Brian Desmond Hurst, who took no formal credit. The picture was adapted from the play Caesar and Cleopatra (1901) by George Bernard Shaw, produced by Independent Producers and Pascal Film Productions and distributed by Eagle-Lion Distributors. Upon release, Caesar and Cleopatra failed to earn back its colossal budget. John Bryan was nominated for an Oscar for Best Art Direction.

Cage Without a Key is a 1975 American made-for-television drama film directed by Buzz Kulik and starring Susan Dey and Sam Bottoms, with Jonelle Allen and Lani O'Grady in supporting roles. The film premiered on the CBS television network the evening of March 14, 1975, later repeating at various times on The CBS Late Movie. The film was released on VHS under the title Imprisoned Women. Cage Without a Key was filmed at Las Palmas School for Girls in Commerce, California, now known as the Dorothy Kirby Center. It was a juvenile detention center, not an actual women's prison. Many of the extras were actual inmates. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:imdbId <OBJ> 0072756 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Buzz_Kulik <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Sony_Pictures_Television <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Robert_Mintz <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Buzz_Kulik <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Sam_Bottoms <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Anne_Bloom <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Katherine_Helmond <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Lani_O'Grady <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cage_Without_a_Key <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Susan_Dey <EOT>

Cairo is a 1942 musical comedy film made by MGM and Loew's, and directed by W. S. Van Dyke. The screenplay was written by John McClain, based on an idea by Ladislas Fodor about a news reporter shipwrecked in a torpedo attack, who teams up with a Hollywood singer and her maid to foil Nazi spies. The music score is by Herbert Stothart. This film was Jeanette MacDonald's last film on her MGM contract. The film was poorly received upon its initial release. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1942_film) <PRED> dbo:imdbId <OBJ> 0034565 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1942_film) <PRED> dbo:releaseDate <OBJ> 1942-08-17 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1942_film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:W._S._Van_Dyke <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1942_film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:James_E._Newcom <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1942_film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Herbert_Stothart <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1942_film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Joseph_L._Mankiewicz <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1942_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Robert_Young_(actor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1942_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jeanette_MacDonald <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cairo_(1942_film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Ladislas_Fodor <EOT>

California Mail is a 1936 American Western film directed by Noel M. Smith and written by Roy Chanslor and Harold Buckley. The film stars Dick Foran, Linda Perry, Edmund Cobb, Milton Kibbee, Tom Brower and James Farley. The film was released by Warner Bros. on November 14, 1936. It was the fourth of 12 B-westerns Foran made for the studio over a two-year period, and is noteworthy for giving ubiquitous bit player Cobb a rare co-starring role as the chief villain. Roy Rogers makes an early, uncredited appearance as the square dance caller. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:imdbId <OBJ> 0027414 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Ted_D._McCord <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Noel_M._Smith <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Warner_Bros. <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Howard_Jackson_(composer) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Bryan_Foy <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Edmund_Cobb <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:James_Farley_(actor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Dick_Foran <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Milton_Kibbee <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Harold_Buckley <EOT>

California's Forgotten Children is an American feature documentary directed by Melody C. Miller. Winning Best Documentary at the 2018 Soho International Film Festival, the film follows a diverse group of resilient survivors who have overcome commercial sexual exploitation of children and are changing the world by ensuring no child is left behind. The film features stories from Time 100 Most Influential People Withelma "T" Ortiz Walker Pettigrew, attorney Carissa Phelps, academic scholar Minh Dang, activist Leah Albright-Byrd, therapist Nikolaos Al-Khadra, and educator Rachel Thomas, M. Ed. The film supports the stories of survivors with current statistics and perspectives of sexual exploitation from professionals in social services, law enforcement, advocates, and child welfare; such as California Against Slavery, Coalition to Abolish Slavery and Trafficking, Saving Innocence, Motivating, Inspiring, Supporting & Serving Sexually Exploited Youth, National Center for Youth Law , Oakland Police Department, Los Angeles Police Department, Runaway Girl Inc., Nancy O'Malley District Attorney for Alameda County, iEmpathize, Bay Area Women Against Rape, Survivor Alliance, SHADE Movement, Heat Watch, Sowers Education Group, Bridget's Dream, and many more. The documentary focuses on those who were wrongfully criminalized in the judicial system; manipulated and coerced by family, friends, and caretakers; and exploited by multiple slavery industries. On June 26, 2019, the film screened at the United States Senate to educate policy makers implementing laws to combat human trafficking. It was honored at the United State of Women Summit in May 2018. Internationally through film festivals, community screenings, and schools, the documentary continues to educate audiences and mobilize action to help victims of child sex trafficking. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California's_Forgotten_Children <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Carissa_Phelps <EOT>

It was released in France and Belgium on 12 April 2006.
Cab Calloway's Jitterbug Party is a 1935 American musical short film which was released by Paramount Pictures (later sold to U.M. & M. TV Corporation). Cabiria is a 1914 Italian epic silent film, directed by Giovanni Pastrone and shot in Turin. The film is set in ancient Sicily, Carthage, and Cirta during the period of the Second Punic War (218–202 BC). It follows a melodramatic main plot about an abducted little girl, Cabiria, and features an eruption of Mount Etna, heinous religious rituals in Carthage, the alpine trek of Hannibal, Archimedes' defeat of the Roman fleet at the Siege of Syracuse and Scipio maneuvering in North Africa. Apart from being a classic on its own terms, the film is also notable for being the first film in which the long-running film character Maciste makes his debut. According to Martin Scorsese, in this work Pastrone invented the epic movie and deserves credit for many of the innovations often attributed to D.W. Griffith and Cecil B. DeMille. Among those was the extensive use of a moving camera, thus freeing the feature-length narrative film from "static gaze". The historical background and characters in the story are taken from Livy's Ab Urbe Condita (written ca. 27–25 BC). In addition, the script of Cabiria was partially based on Gustave Flaubert's 1862 novel Salammbo and Emilio Salgari's 1908 novel Cartagine in fiamme (Carthage in Flames). It was the first film shown at the White House, having been viewed on the South Lawn, by the President, First Lady, Vice President, his wife, members of the Cabinet and their wives, due to the summer heat in June 1914. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Eugenio_Bava <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Segundo_de_Chomon <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Giovanni_Pastrone <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Silent_film <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Intertitles <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Ildebrando_Pizzetti <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Manlio_Mazza <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Giovanni_Pastrone <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Bartolomeo_Pagano <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Gabriele_D'Annunzio <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cabiria <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Giovanni_Pastrone <EOT>

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:imdbId <OBJ> 0027414 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Ted_D._McCord <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Noel_M._Smith <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Warner_Bros. <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Howard_Jackson_(composer) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Bryan_Foy <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Edmund_Cobb <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:James_Farley_(actor) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Dick_Foran <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Milton_Kibbee <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California_Mail <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Harold_Buckley <EOT> <RDF2Text>	California Mail is a 1936 American Western film directed by Noel M. Smith and written by Roy Chanslor and Harold Buckley. The film stars Dick Foran, Linda Perry, Edmund Cobb, Milton Kibbee, Tom Brower and James Farley. The film was released by Warner Bros. on November 14, 1936. It was the fourth of 12 B-westerns Foran made for the studio over a two-year period, and is noteworthy for giving ubiquitous bit player Cobb a rare co-starring role as the chief villain. Roy Rogers makes an early, uncredited appearance as the square dance caller.

Cagefighter: Worlds Collide is a 2020 British-American action sports film written and directed by Jesse Quinones. Starring Alex Montagnani, Jonathan Good, Gina Gershon, Jay Reso, and Chuck Liddell, the film follows a successful MMA champion who agrees to defend his championship against a professional wrestler. Vignola, and starring Gilda Gray. The film was considered a rival to Paramount's own Underworld released later in 1927. Cabaret is now presumed to be a lost film. It was the winner of the Photoplay award in 1927.

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Noir <PRED> dbo:country <OBJ> dbr:South_Korea <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Noir <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:Jung_Sung-il_(director) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Noir <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Jung_Yu-mi_(actress_born_1983) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Noir <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Moon_Jeong-hee <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Noir <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Shin_Ha-kyun <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafe_Noir <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Jung_Sung-il_(director) <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Cafe Noir (Korean: 카페 느와르; RR: Ka-pe-neu-wa-reu) is a 2009 South Korean romance melodrama film starring Shin Ha-kyun, Moon Jeong-hee, Kim Hye-na and Jung Yu-mi. Written and directed by first-time director Jung Sung-il, a well regarded film critic-turned-director, it is a contemplation on love and heartbreak largely based on two works of literature - Johann Wolfgang von Goethe's The Sorrows of Young Werther and Fyodor Dostoyevsky's White Nights. The critically acclaimed work debuted at the 66th Venice Film Festival in 2009, and Jung was nominated for New Talent Grand Pix at the 2010 Copenhagen International Film Festival.

Cafard is a 2015 French-Dutch-Belgian animated war film written and directed by Jan Bultheel. The film tells the story of a boxer, Jean Mordant (based on the real-life Henri Herd, known as Constant le Marin), who joins the Belgian Expeditionary Corps which is sent to the Russian Empire during World War I in order to avenge the rape of his daughter by German soldiers in Occupied Belgium. <Text2RDF>	<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafard <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:France <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Cafard <PRED> dbo:language <OBJ> dbr:Netherlands <EOT>

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:California's_Forgotten_Children <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Carissa_Phelps <EOT> <RDF2Text>	California's Forgotten Children is an American feature documentary directed by Melody C. Miller. Winning Best Documentary at the 2018 Soho International Film Festival, the film follows a diverse group of resilient survivors who have overcome commercial sexual exploitation of children and are changing the world by ensuring no child is left behind. The film features stories from Time 100 Most Influential People Withelma "T" Ortiz Walker Pettigrew, attorney Carissa Phelps, academic scholar Minh Dang, activist Leah Albright-Byrd, therapist Nikolaos Al-Khadra, and educator Rachel Thomas, M. Ed. The film supports the stories of survivors with current statistics and perspectives of sexual exploitation from professionals in social services, law enforcement, advocates, and child welfare; such as California Against Slavery, Coalition to Abolish Slavery and Trafficking, Saving Innocence, Motivating, Inspiring, Supporting & Serving Sexually Exploited Youth, National Center for Youth Law , Oakland Police Department, Los Angeles Police Department, Runaway Girl Inc., Nancy O'Malley District Attorney for Alameda County, iEmpathize, Bay Area Women Against Rape, Survivor Alliance, SHADE Movement, Heat Watch, Sowers Education Group, Bridget's Dream, and many more. The documentary focuses on those who were wrongfully criminalized in the judicial system; manipulated and coerced by family, friends, and caretakers; and exploited by multiple slavery industries. On June 26, 2019, the film screened at the United States Senate to educate policy makers implementing laws to combat human trafficking. It was honored at the United State of Women Summit in May 2018. Internationally through film festivals, community screenings, and schools, the documentary continues to educate audiences and mobilize action to help victims of child sex trafficking.

<SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:imdbId <OBJ> 0042296 <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:cinematography <OBJ> dbr:Carl_E._Guthrie <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:director <OBJ> dbr:John_Cromwell_(director) <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:distributor <OBJ> dbr:Warner_Bros. <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:editing <OBJ> dbr:Owen_Marks <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:musicComposer <OBJ> dbr:Max_Steiner <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:producer <OBJ> dbr:Jerry_Wald <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Betty_Garde <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Hope_Emerson <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Eleanor_Parker <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Ellen_Corby <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:starring <OBJ> dbr:Agnes_Moorehead <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Bernard_C._Schoenfeld <EOT> <SOT> <SUBJ> dbr:Caged_(1950_film) <PRED> dbo:writer <OBJ> dbr:Virginia_Kellogg <EOT> <RDF2Text>	Caged is a 1950 American women-in-prison film noir directed by John Cromwell and starring Eleanor Parker, Agnes Moorehead, Betty Garde, Hope Emerson, and Ellen Corby. It was nominated for three Academy Awards. The film portrays the story of a young newlywed sent to prison for armed robbery. Her brutal experiences while incarcerated, along with the killing of her husband, transform her from a meek, naive woman into a hardened convict. The film's subplot includes massive prison corruption. Caged was adapted by Virginia Kellogg from the story "Women Without Men" by Kellogg and Bernard C. Schoenfeld. The studio had originally intended the film to be a vehicle for Bette Davis and Joan Crawford, but reportedly Davis had said she did not want to make a "dyke movie" (a film with lesbian content) and turned it down.
